Muhammad said: And whoever's guardian is killed intentionally, then the guardian cuts the hand of the killer, then forgives — whether qisas was already decreed for him or not — then upon the one who cut the hand is the diyah of the hand according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said: nothing is on him, because he has taken his right, so he is not liable. And this is because the guardian is entitled to the destruction of the life with all its parts. Translation: Muhammad said: And a person whose guardian is killed intentionally, then the guardian cuts the hand of the killer, then forgives — whether qisas was decreed or not — then the cutter of the hand is liable for the diyah of the hand according to Abu Hanifa. Sahibayn said: nothing is on him, because he has taken his right, so he is not liable. And this is because the guardian is entitled to take life with all its parts. Commentary: Zayd kills Bakr intentionally, so qisas is due. Bakr's son Khalid, the heir, cuts Zayd's hand before or after decree, then Khalid forgives Zayd. In this case, Imam Abu Hanifa says:
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute: the guardian of a murder victim cuts off the murderer's hand (instead of taking life qisas) and then forgives the murderer. Abu Hanifa rules that the guardian must pay diyah for the hand he cut, because he acted without proper right to cut the hand (since his right was to the whole life, not a limb). Sahibayn argue that the guardian already took his right by cutting the hand; since it was part of the life he was entitled to destroy, no liability arises. The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the guardian pays hand diyah; under Sahibayn, no payment. The text cuts off but the position is clear.

Key Terms
دية اليد (diyat al-yad): The blood money for a hand, which is half of full diyah (i.e., 50 camels or equivalent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The guardian must pay full diyah of life.

Key Takeaway
The right to qisas (life) does not automatically permit taking a limb; exceeding that right creates liability for diyah according to Abu Hanifa.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Diya for Cutting Hand Before Qisas Forgiveness
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for diya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding liability for diya when a guardian cuts the offender's hand instead of executing qisas, and identify the practical consequence of the disagreement.

Core Idea
A guardian with a right to kill who cuts a limb instead exceeds his right; Abu Hanifa holds him liable for diya, the Sahibayn do not.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a nuanced debate between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two eminent disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The question is whether a guardian who, instead of executing the death penalty (qisas), cuts off the offender's hand becomes liable for blood money (diya). The dispute hinges on the precise scope of the guardian's right and the concept of 'recovering other than one's right' (استيفاء غير الحق).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Clearly describe the hypothetical: a guardian (wali) has the right of qisas for murder against a convicted offender. Instead of killing him, the guardian cuts off his hand. The wound later heals. The question is whether the guardian must pay diya for the hand.
The guardian did not forgive the qisas; he simply performed a different act.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Recall that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that no diya is owed because the guardian was entitled to kill the offender, and cutting a limb is a lesser act within that right. They support their view with examples: if the wound kills, or if he cuts the hand then neck, or if he has qisas for a limb and cuts fingers then forgives, there is no liability.
Their reasoning: if killing would not incur liability, lesser harm should also not.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the guardian's right is specifically to kill (qisas of the soul). Cutting a hand is an act beyond his right, so he is liable. However, diya is not due immediately because if the wound spreads and kills, the guardian would have executed his right. Therefore, we wait for healing: if the wound heals, diya is wajib; if the offender dies, no liability.
He also invokes the principle 'necessity is measured by its extent' (الضرورة تتقدر بقدرها) to limit the guardian's ownership of qisas to the specific act of killing.
4
Determine the practical consequence and tarjih
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that under Abu Hanifa's view, the guardian must pay diya if the hand heals; under the Sahibayn's view, he does not. The text does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, but the commentary appears to favor Abu Hanifa's argument. In practice, the Hanafi school often follows Abu Hanifa on this stricter point.
Understanding this dispute sharpens one's ability to apply the principle of qisas strictly: the right is defined by the crime, not by general vengeance.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵
1-2
كتاب الجنايات
ہیں کہ خالد کو زید کے ہاتھ کی دیت دینی پڑے گی ۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ نہیں دینی پڑے گی ۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خالد نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے اس میں دیت کا کیا مطلب ہے اگر وہ اسے قصاص میں قتل کرتا تب بھی جائز تھا اور اس پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوتا لہذا یہاں پر بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین نے مزید شواہد پیش کرتے ہوئے فرمایا۔
صاحبین کے استشہادات
ولهذا لـولـم يـعف لا يضمنه وكذا اذا سرى ومابرأ او ماعفا وما سرى أو قطع ثم حزر قبته قبل البرأ او بعده وصار كما اذا كان له قصاص في الطرف فقطع اصابعه ثم عفا لا يضمن الاصابع ترجمہ اسی وجہ سے اگر ولی معاف نہ کرتا تو ضامن نہ ہوتا اور ایسے ہی جب کہ سرایت کر جائے اور اچھا نہ ہو یا وہ معاف نہ کرتا اور سرایت نہ کرتا یا ہاتھ کاٹ دیتا پھر اچھا ہونے سے پہلے یا اس کے بعد اس کی گردن کاٹ دیتا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ ولی کے لئے قصاص فی الطرف ہو پس اس نے مجرم کی انگلیاں کاٹ دیں پھر معاف کر دیا تو ولی انگلیوں کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح چار جزئیات صاحبین نے استشہاد میں پیش کی ہیں۔
1 ولی نے ہاتھ کاٹنے کے بعد معاف نہیں کیا خواہ زخم سرایت کرے یا نہ کرے ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ (۲) معاف نہیں کیا اور زخم سرایت کر گیا اور مر گیا یہاں بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
(۳) نہ زخم نے سرایت کی اور نہ اس نے معاف کیا یہاں بھی ضمان نہ ہو گا ۔
ہاتھ کاٹا پھر گردن کاٹ دی ابھی اچھا ہو یا نہ ہوا ہو تو ان تمام صورتوں میں قاطع پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔
اسی طرح صورت مذکورہ میں بھی دیت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے زید نے بکر کا ہاتھ عمداً کاٹا ہو جس کی وجہ سے زید پر ہاتھ کا قصاص واجب تھا لیکن بکر نے صرف زید کی انگلیاں کاٹ دیں اور اس کو معاف کر دیا تو بکر پر انگلیوں کی دیت واجب نہ ہوگی اسی طرح صورت مذکورہ کا بھی حکم ہوگا۔
صاحبین کی دلیل ختم ہوگئی ہے وفیہ تفصیل فی الکفایہ۔
امام صاحب کی دلیل
قتلا
وله انه استوفى غير حقه لان حقه في القتل وهذا قطع وابانة وكان القياس إن يجب القصاص الا انه سقط للشبهة فان له ان يتلفه تبعا واذا سقط وجب المال وانما لايجب فى الحال لانه يحتمل ان يصير ـراية فيكون مسـ المـ
ترجمہ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے اپنے حق کے غیر کو وصول کیا ہے اس لئے کہ ولی کا حق تو قتل میں ہے اور یہ کاٹنا اور جدا کرنا ہے اور قیاس یہ تھا کہ قصاص واجب ہو مگر قصاص شبہ کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گیا اس لئے کہ ولی کو حق تھا کہ وہ ہاتھ کو تبعیت کے طریقہ تلف کرتا اور جب قصاص ساقط ہو گیا تو مال واجب ہوگا اور مال فی الحال واجب نہ ہو گا ( بلکہ ہاتھ اچھا ہونے پر ) اس لئے کہ احتمال ہے کہ قطع سرایت کی وجہ سے قتل ہو جائے تو ولی اپنے حق کو وصول کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵
تشریح امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چونکہ ولی کا حق قتل تھا نہ کہ قطع اور اس نے اپنے حق کا غیر وصول کیا ہے تو اس پر ہاتھ کی دیت واجب ہوگی بلکہ قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ تھا کہ قصاص واجب ہوتا لیکن چونکہ ولی کو حق حاصل تھا کہ وہ مجرم کو قتل کرے اور جب وہ قتل کرتا تو اس کے ہاتھ بھی تلف ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے اس میں شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور شبہ کی وجہ سے بجائے قصاص کے مال واجب ہوا لیکن ولی کے ہاتھ کاٹنے کی وجہ سے اگر وہ مجرم مر جائے تو چونکہ ولی نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے لہذا ولی پر کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہو گا۔ اور چونکہ احتمال ہے کہ قطع ید سرایت کر کے قتل تک نوبت پہنچ جائے اس وجہ سے ولی سے فی الحال ہاتھ کی دیت وصول نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ بلکہ زخم اچھا ہونے کا انتظار کیا جائے گا اگر ٹھیک ہو گیا تو دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر ٹھیک نہ ہوا بلکہ مر گیا تو واجب نہ ہوگی۔
امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل کا تکملہ
وملك القصاص في النفس ضروري لا يظهر الا عند الاستيفاء او العفو أو الاعتياض لما انه تصرف فيه فاما قبل ذلك لم يظهر لعدم الضرورة بخلاف ما اذا سرى لانه استيفاء ترجمہ اور ملک قصاص نفس میں ضروری ہے تو یہ ملک ظاہر نہ ہوگی استیفاء یا عفو یا عوض لینے کے وقت اس لئے کہ یہ ان میں سے ہم ایک ) ملک میں تصرف ہے پس بہر حال اس سے پہلے ضرورت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ملک ظاہر نہ ہوگی ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ سرایت کر جائے اس لئے کہ یہ وصول کرنا ہے۔
تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل کا دوسرا پرزہ ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قاعدہ مقررہ ہے۔ الضرورة تتقد ربقدر الضرورة ، كج چیز بر بنا و ضرورت ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ ضرورت کی حد تک ہی رہتی ہے۔
پھر یہ مجرم آزاد ہے اور محترم ہے اس کے باوجود بھی ولی کے لئے ملک قصاص کو جو ثابت کیا گیا ہے وہ بر بنا ضرورت ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ یہ ملک قصاص بر بنا ضرورت ہے اس لئے اس کا اثبات صرف اس جگہ کیا جائے گا جب کہ ولی اپنا حق وصول کرے اور اس کے حق کی وصولیابی کی تین صورتیں ہیں: (۱) قصاص (۲) معاف کر دے (۳) اس کا عوض لے لے کیونکہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں سے جس کو بھی ولی اختیا کرے گا وہ اپنی ملک میں تصرف ہو گا لہذا یہ اس کا تصرف معتبر ہو گا لیکن جہاں ان تینوں امور میں سے کچھ بھی نہ ہو تو وہاں ضرورت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ملک قصاص جو امر ضروری ہے ثابت نہ ہوگا اور جب ملک قصاص نہ ہوا تو غیر حق میں تصرف ہوا لہذا اس بیجا تصرف کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان دینا واجب ہوگا۔ اور قطع ید سرایت کر کے قتل بن جائے تو اب چونکہ اس نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے لہذا اب اس پر کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
امام صاحب کا صاحبین کے استشہاد ثالث کا جواب
واما اذا لم يعف وما سرى قلنا انما يتبين كونه قطعا بغير حق بالبرء حتى لو قطع وما عفا وبرأ الصحيح ان على هذا الخلاف
Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 15. Book of Homicides. That Khalid would have to pay the diya of Zaid's hand. And the Sahibayn said: no, he will not have to pay. The Sahibayn's evidence is that Khalid recovered his own right, what meaning does diya have here? If he had killed him in qisas, it would have been permissible and no liability would be on him, so here too liability is not wajib. The Sahibayn presented further evidence: 'Therefore if he had not forgiven, he would not be liable; similarly if it spreads and does not heal, or if he did not forgive and it did not spread, or if he cut his hand then cut his neck before or after healing; and it becomes like when he had qisas for a limb and cut his fingers then forgave, he is not liable for the fingers.' Explanation: The Sahibayn presented four examples: 1) He cut the hand then did not forgive, whether the wound spreads or not, he is not liable. 2) He did not forgive and the wound spread and he died, here also liability is not wajib. 3) The wound did not spread and he did not forgive, here also no liability. 4) He cut the hand then cut the neck, whether healed or not, the cutter is not liable in all these cases. Similarly, in the mentioned case, diya is not wajib. And its exact example is Zaid intentionally cut Bakr's hand, which made qisas of the hand wajib on Zaid, but Bakr only cut Zaid's fingers and forgave him, so diya of the fingers is not wajib on Bakr; similarly the judgment will be for the mentioned case. The Sahibayn's evidence is finished; there is detail in al-Kifayah. Imam Sahib's evidence: 'And his argument is that he recovered other than his right, because his right is in killing, and this is cutting and severing; and analogically qisas would be wajib, but it is dropped due to doubt, because he has the right to destroy it as a consequence; and when it is dropped, property becomes wajib; and it is not wajib immediately because it is possible that it becomes...' Translation: And Abu Hanifa's argument is that he recovered other than his right, because the guardian's right is to kill, and this is cutting and separating; and analogically qisas would be wajib, but qisas was dropped due to doubt, because the guardian had the right to destroy the hand as a consequence; and when qisas is dropped, property becomes wajib; and property is not wajib immediately (but upon healing of the hand) because there is a possibility that the cutting spreads and causes death, then the guardian would have recovered his right. Explanation of Imam Abu Hanifa's argument: Since the guardian's right was killing, not cutting, and he recovered other than his right, so diya of the hand will be wajib on him. Indeed, the requirement of analogy was that qisas would be wajib, but since the guardian had the right to kill the criminal and in killing his hand would also be destroyed, doubt arose, and due to doubt, property became wajib instead of qisas. But if due to the guardian cutting his hand, the criminal dies, since the guardian recovered his right, no liability on him. And since there is a possibility that the cutting of the hand spreads leading to death, the diya of the hand is not collected from the guardian immediately; rather, healing of the wound is awaited: if it heals, diya is wajib; if it does not heal but he dies, it is not wajib. Completion of Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence: 'And ownership of qisas of the soul is necessary; it does not appear except at the time of execution, forgiveness, or taking compensation, because it is a disposal in ownership; before that it does not appear due to lack of necessity, contrary to when it spreads, because that is execution.' Translation: And ownership of qisas of the soul is necessary; this ownership does not appear except at the time of execution, forgiveness, or taking compensation, because this is a disposal in ownership. In any case, before that, due to lack of necessity, ownership does not appear. Contrary to the case when it spreads, because that is recovery. Explanation: This is the second part of Imam Abu Hanifa's argument, the summary of which is that the established principle is 'Necessity is measured by its extent'. Whatever is established due to necessity remains only to the extent of necessity. Then this criminal is free and inviolable; despite that, the ownership of qisas established for the guardian is due to necessity. But since this ownership of qisas is due to necessity, its establishment will only be when the guardian recovers his right. Recovery of his right has three forms: (1) qisas, (2) forgiveness, (3) taking compensation. Because whichever of these two forms the guardian chooses, it will be a disposal in his ownership, so his disposal is valid. But where none of these three matters occur, then due to lack of necessity, ownership of qisas, which is a necessary matter, will not be established. When ownership of qisas is not established, then there was disposal in other than his right, so due to this improper disposal, liability to pay compensation becomes wajib. And if the cutting of the hand spreads and becomes killing, then since he has recovered his right, no liability will be on him. Imam Sahib's response to the Sahibayn's third evidence: 'As for when he did not forgive and it did not spread, we say that it only becomes known that it was a cutting without right upon healing, so that if he cut and forgave and it healed, the correct view is that there is a dispute on this.'
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding a scenario in the Book of Homicides. The case: a person (the 'wali' or guardian) has a right of qisas (retaliation) against an offender for killing, but instead of killing, he cuts off the offender's hand. Later, the wound heals or the offender dies from the wound. The question is whether the guardian must pay diya (blood money) for the hand. The Sahibayn argue that no diya is due because the guardian was entitled to qisas (death), and since cutting the hand is a lesser act within his right, and if he had killed, there would be no liability, so here also no liability. They present four examples: (1) cutting the hand without forgiveness – no liability; (2) wound spreads and kills – no liability; (3) no forgiveness and no spread – no liability; (4) cutting hand then cutting neck – no liability. They analogize to a case where the guardian only has qisas for a limb and cuts the offender's fingers then forgives – no liability for the fingers. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees. His reasoning: the guardian's right was specifically to kill (qisas for murder), not to cut limbs. By cutting the hand, he exceeded his right, so he should be liable. Analogically, qisas would be required, but it is dropped due to shubha (doubt) because the guardian had the right to destroy the hand as part of the execution (if he killed, the hand would be destroyed anyway). So instead of qisas, property (diya) becomes wajib. However, diya is not due immediately because if the wound spreads and kills the offender, the guardian would have actually executed his qisas right, so no liability. Therefore, we wait for the wound to heal: if it heals, diya is due; if the offender dies, no diya. The guardian's ownership of qisas is 'daruri' (necessary) and only manifests upon actual execution, forgiveness, or taking compensation. Before that, there is no established ownership, so cutting the hand is an act without right, requiring compensation. The text also includes a response to the Sahibayn's third example: if he did not forgive and the wound did not spread, we say the nature of the act as an unjustified cutting becomes clear only upon healing. The correct view is that there is a dispute on this, implying the commentary sides with the need to await healing. This passage is from a later commentary (Ashraf al-Hidaya) on al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, which itself represents the Zahir al-Riwayah. The dispute is intra-madhhab, and the commentary seems to favor Abu Hanifa's view, though the mufta bihi may be the Sahibayn's view in some later fatwas? The text does not explicitly state the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or intentional injury; the right of the victim or guardian to exact equivalent harm upon the offender.
دیت (diya): Blood money paid in compensation for homicide or injury; it substitutes for qisas when qisas is not carried out or is waived.
ولی (wali): The legal guardian of the victim in crimes of qisas; the person entitled to demand qisas or accept diya.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation; in this context, liability for diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the guardian liable to pay diya for cutting the offender's hand when he had a right of qisas for murder?
A) Because cutting the hand is a graver crime than killing.
B) Because the guardian's right was specifically to kill, not to cut limbs; thus he recovered other than his right.
C) Because the guardian's ownership of qisas is absolute and immediate, so any act before execution is a crime.
D) Because the Sahibayn's evidence was weak.

Key Takeaway
The right to qisas is strictly proportional to the crime; any act beyond that right incurs liability, but the timing of liability depends on the outcome of the injury.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Liability of the Wali for Cutting the Murderer's Hand: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof and response to Sahibayn on liability for cutting hand before death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on diyat when the wali cuts the murderer's hand, explain his dalil (ownership of qisas is daruri and limited to three modes), and evaluate the Sahibayn's istishhad and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The wali owns only the life, not the limb; cutting the hand without execution, forgiveness, or compensation is a transgression requiring diyat unless the wound causes death.

In the Hanafi school, there is a detailed debate about the liability of the wali (guardian of a murder victim) when he takes the law into his own hands by cutting off the hand of the murderer before executing the killer. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two famous students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), disagreed on whether the wali must pay blood-money (diyat) if the wound heals or if death results from the injury. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind Imam Abu Hanifa's position and how he refuted the Sahibayn's objections. Understanding this dispute clarifies the limits of the wali's right of retaliation and the role of necessity in Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What exactly is being disputed? The wali cuts the hand of the convicted murderer before executing qisas. Two scenarios: (a) the wound heals, (b) the wound causes death (saraya). Determine the ruling on liability for the hand.
The core question: does the wali's right to the life extend to the limb?
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling and its qiyas basis
Imam's ruling: If wound heals → diyat wajib for the hand. If wound kills → no diyat (act becomes istifa'). The pure qiyas would require qisas (because the wali injured another), but a shubha (doubt) arises from his right to kill, converting qisas to diyat. Understand the role of shubha.
Shubha here is the wali's right to take the life, which creates ambiguity in his act.
3
Analyze Imam's proof (dalil aqli)
Imam's proof: 'Milk al-qisas fil-nafs daruri la yazharu illa 'ind al-istifa' aw al-'afw aw al-i'wad.' The ownership of qisas is a necessary right that only becomes effective in three ways: execution, forgiveness, or taking compensation. Before that, the wali has no right to act on the body. Thus, any act outside these three is a transgression requiring compensation unless it accidentally results in the death (making it retroactively execution).
The principle 'al-darura tuqaddaru bi qadariha' (necessity is measured by its extent) underpins this.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's istishhad and Imam's response
The Sahibayn presented several example cases (istishhad) to argue that in some situations the wali should not be liable. Imam refutes each: (a) third instance: no forgiveness and no spread does not prove right until the wound heals; (b) fourth instance: cutting before healing and slitting neck is istifa', but after healing it is still a transgression; (c) fifth instance: analogy between fingers/palm and limbs/life is flawed because limbs are subordinate to life in every respect.
The istishhad method is used to test a legal principle by applying it to hypotheticals.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practical consequence: Under Imam Abu Hanifa's view, the wali who cuts a limb without proper authority must pay diyat if the wound heals. Under the Sahibayn's likely view, in some cases the wali might avoid diyat even if the wound heals. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; both positions are valid, but the dominant view is Imam's.

تشریح امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چونکہ ولی کا حق قتل تھا [؟] کہ قطع اور اس نے اپنے حق کا غیر وصول کیا ہے تو اس پر ہاتھ کی دیت واجب ہوگی بلکہ قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ تھا کہ قصاص واجب ہوتا لیکن چونکہ ولی کوحق حاصل تھا کہ وہ مجرم کو قتل کرے اور جب وہ قتل کو [؟] کا ہاتھ بھی تلف ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے اس میں شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور شبہ کی وجہ سے بجائے قصاص کے مال واجب ہوا لیکن ولی کے ہاتھ کاٹنے کی وجہ سے اگر وہ مجرم مر جائے تو چونکہ ولی نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے لہذا ولی پر کوئی منعمان واجب نہ ہو گا۔ اور چونکہ احتمال ہے کہ قطع ید سرایت کر کے قتل تک نوبت پہنچ جائے اس وجہ سے ولی سے فی الحال ہاتھ کی دیت وصول نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ بلکہ زخم اچھا ہونے کا انتظار کیا جائے گا اگر ٹھیک ہو گیا تو دیت واجب ہوگی اور اگر ٹھیک نہ ہوا بلکہ مرگیا تو واجب نہ ہوگی۔

امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل کا تکملہ

وملك القصاص في النفس ضروري لا يظهر الا عند الاستيفاء او العفو أو الاعتياض لما انه تصرف فيه فاما قبل ذلك لم يظهر لعدم الضرورة بخلاف ما اذا سرى لانه استيفاء ترجمہ اور ملک قصاص نفس میں ضروری ہے تو یہ ملک ظاہر نہ ہوگی استیفاء یا عفو یا عوض لینے کے وقت اس لئے کہ یہ ان میں سے ہم ایک ) ملک میں تصرف ہے پس بہر حال اس سے پہلے ضرورت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ملک ظاہر نہ ہوگی ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ سرایت کر جائے اس لئے کہ یہ وصول کرنا ہے۔

تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل کا دوسرا پرزہ ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قاعدہ مقررہ ہے۔ الضرورة تتقد ربقدر الضرورة ، كج چیز بر بنا و ضرورت ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ ضرورت کی حد تک ہی رہتی ہے۔

پھر یہ مجرم آزاد ہے اور محترم ہے اس کے باوجود بھی ولی کے لئے ملک قصاص کو جو ثابت کیا گیا ہے وہ بر بنا ضرورت ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ یہ ملک قصاص بر بنا ضرورت ہے اس لئے اس کا اثبات صرف اس جگہ کیا جائے گا جب کہ ولی اپنا حق وصول کرے اور اس کے حق کی وصولیابی کی تین صورتیں ہیں: (۱) قصاص (۲) معاف کر دے (۳) اس کا عوض لے لے کیونکہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں سے جس کو بھی ولی اختیا کرے گا وہ اپنی ملک میں تصرف ہو گا لہذا یہ اس کا تصرف معتبر ہو گا لیکن جہاں ان تینوں امور میں سے کچھ بھی نہ ہو تو وہاں ضرورت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ملک قصاص جو امر ضروری ہے ثابت نہ ہوگا اور جب ملک قصاص نہ ہوا تو غیر حق میں تصرف ہوا لہذا اس بیجا تصرف کی وجہ سے اس پر ضمان دینا واجب ہوگا۔ اور قطع ید سرایت کر کے قتل بن جائے تو اب چونکہ اس نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے لہذا اب اس پر کوئی ممان واجب نہ ہوگا۔

امام صاحب کا صاحبین کے استشہاد ثالث کا جواب

واما اذا لم يعف وما سرى قلنا انما يتبين كونه قطعا بغير حق بالبرء حتى لو قطع وما عفا وبرأ الصحيح ان على هذا الخلاف

ترجمہ اور بہر حال جب کہ اس نے معاف نہیں کیا اور نہ زخم نے سرایت کی تو ہم کہیں گے کہ اس قطع کا بغیر حق کے قطع ہونا برأت س ظاہر ہو گا یہاں تک کہ اگر ولی نے ہاتھ کاٹا اور معاف نہیں کیا اور اچھا ہو گیا تو صحیح یہ ہے کہ صورت اختلافی ہے۔ تشریح یہاں سے امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ اے صاحبین ہم نےچار جزئیات استشہاد میں پیش کی ہیں تو ان میں سے تیسری جزئی سے آپ کا استشہاد درست نہیں تیسری جزئی یہ تھی کہ نہ ولی نے معاف کیا اور نہ زخم نے سرایت کی تو یہاں دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ بات صحیح ہے مگر اس سے آپ کا استدلال درست نہیں اس لئے کہ سرایت نہ کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ابھی زخم کی پوزیشن کیا رخ اختیار کرنے والی ہے اس کا کچھ پتہ نہیں چلا مگر ابھی زخم اچھا تو نہیں ہوا۔

جب زخم ابھی اچھا نہیں ہوا تو احتمال ہے کہ مجرم اس زخم کی وجہ سے مرجائے تو پھر ولی پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ ناحق قطع اس وقت کہلاتا ہے کہ زخم اچھا ہو گیا ہوتا اور یہاں تو اچھا نہیں ہوا البتہ ابھی اس نے سرایت نہیں کی تو احتمال تو ہے کہ سرایت کر جائے اس وجہ سے ابھی دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ لہذا اس جزئی استدلال درست نہیں رہا۔ ور نہ اگر ولی مجرم کا ہاتھ کاٹ دے اور اس نے معاف بھی نہ کیا ہو اور زخم اچھا ہو گیا ہو تو امام صاحب یہاں بھی دیت کو واجب کرتے ہیں۔

خلاصہ کلام تیسری جزئی سے استدلال ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔

چوتھے استشہاد کا جواب

واذا قطع ثم حز رقبته قبل البرء فهو استيفاء ولو حز بعد البرء فهو على هذا الخلاف هو الصحيح و صابع وان كانت تابعة قياما بالكف فالكف تابعة لها غرضا بخلاف الطرف لانها تابعة للنفس من كل وجه . ترجمہ اور جب کہ ولی نے ہاتھ کاٹا ہو پھر اچھا ہونے سے پہلے اس کی گردن کاٹ دی ہو تو یہ استیفاء ہے اور اگر اچھا ہونے کے بعد کائی ہو تو یہ اس اختلاف پر ہے یہی صحیح ہے اور انگلیاں قیام و تحصل کے اعتبار سے اگر چہ ہتھیلی کا تابع ہیں پس ہتھیلی انگلیوں کے تابع ہے۔ غرض کے لحاظ سے بخلاف طرف کے اس لئے کہ یہ (اطراف ) ہر اعتبار سے نفس کے تابع ہیں۔ تشریح امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں اسی طرح اے صاحبین آپ کا چوتھی جزئی سے مطلقاً استدلال بھی سیج نہیں کیونکہ وہ تفصیل طلب ہے اگر ولی نے ہاتھ کاٹنے کے بعد تندرستی سے پہلے ہی اس کی گردن کاٹ دی ہو تو یہاں دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ ولی نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے۔ لیکن اگر اچھا ہونے کے بعد گردن کائی ہو تو امام صاحب یہاں بھی وہی فرماتے ہیں کہ دیت واجب ہوگی لہذا اس سے استدلال درست نہ ہوگا۔

اور اسے صاحبین تم نے جو پانچویں جزئی استشہاد میں مثال دیتے ہوئے پیش کی تھی اس سے بھی استدلال صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک اعتبار سے انگلیاں ہتھیلی کے تابع ہیں اور ایک اعتبار سے ہتھیلی انگلیوں کے تابع ہے، اول کی تبعیت اس وجہ سے ہے کہ بغیر ہتھیلی کے انگلیوں کا قیام نہ ہوگا اور ہتھیلی اس لئے تابع ہے کہ ہتھیلی کے بغیر انگلیوں سے پکڑا نہیں جائے گا۔
Book of Homicides. If death occurs due to [the wound] spreading, then the guardian will be one who receives his right. Explanation: The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that since the guardian's right was to kill, [and] he cut [the hand] and he received his right other than [the actual execution], then upon him the blood money for the hand becomes obligatory. Rather, what analogy (qiyas) required was that qisas would be obligatory, but since the guardian had the right to kill the criminal, and when he [?] to kill, the hand also perishes. Due to this, doubt (shubha) arose, and due to doubt, wealth (mal) became obligatory instead of qisas. But due to the guardian cutting off the hand, if that criminal dies, then since the guardian has received his right, therefore no liability (daman) is obligatory upon the guardian. And because there is a possibility that the cutting of the hand may spread and reach the point of death, for this reason, the blood money for the hand will not be collected from the guardian immediately. Rather, the healing of the wound will be awaited; if it heals, then the blood money becomes obligatory, and if it does not heal but he dies, then it does not become obligatory. Completion of Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: 'And ownership of qisas regarding life is necessary; it does not appear except at the time of execution (istifa'), or forgiveness ('afw), or taking compensation (i'wad), because it is a disposition (tasarruf) in it. As for before that, it does not appear due to lack of necessity, contrary to when it spreads, because it is execution.' Translation: And ownership of qisas for life is necessary, so this ownership does not appear except at the time of execution, forgiveness, or taking compensation, because this is a disposition in ownership. Therefore, before that, due to lack of necessity, ownership does not appear, contrary to the case when it spreads, because that is receiving [the right]. Explanation: This is the second part of Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, the summary of which is that the established rule is: necessity is measured by the extent of necessity. Whatever is established based on necessity remains only to the extent of necessity. Then this criminal is free and inviolable; despite that, the ownership of qisas established for the guardian is based on necessity. But since this ownership of qisas is based on necessity, its establishment will be only in the place where the guardian receives his right. And there are three forms of receiving his right: (1) qisas, (2) he forgives, (3) he takes compensation for it, because whichever of these two [sic] forms the guardian chooses, it will be a disposition in his ownership, so this disposition of his will be valid. But when none of these three matters occur, then due to lack of necessity, the ownership of qisas, which is a necessary matter, will not be established. And when ownership of qisas does not occur, then a disposition occurred without right, so due to this improper disposition, it becomes obligatory upon him to provide compensation (daman). And if the cutting of the hand spreads and becomes homicide, then since he has received his right, therefore no liability is obligatory upon him. Imam's response to the Sahibayn's third istishhad: 'And when he did not forgive and it did not spread, we say that it becomes evident that it was a cutting without right upon healing (bar'), to the extent that if he cut, did not forgive, and it healed, the correct [view] is that it is upon this dispute.' Translation: And in any case when he did not forgive and the wound did not spread, we will say that this cutting becomes evident as a cutting without right upon healing, to the extent that if the guardian cut the hand and did not forgive and it healed, the correct [view] is that it is a disputed case. Explanation: From here Imam says: O Sahibayn, we have presented four instances in the istishhad. Among them, your istishhad from the third instance is not correct. The third instance was: the guardian did not forgive and the wound did not spread, so here blood money would not be obligatory. That statement is correct, but your inference from it is not correct, because the meaning of not spreading is that the direction the wound will take has not yet been determined, but the wound has not yet healed. When the wound has not yet healed, there is a possibility that the criminal may die from this wound, and then there would be no liability upon the guardian. In summary, a cutting without right is called such only when the wound has healed, and here it has not healed. However, it has not spread yet, but there is a possibility that it may spread, so for this reason blood money is not obligatory yet. Therefore, this instance does not support your inference. Otherwise, if the guardian cuts the criminal's hand and he did not forgive and the wound healed, then Imam (Abu Hanifa) also makes blood money obligatory here. In summary, the inference from the third instance is not correct. Response to the fourth istishhad: 'And if he cut then slit his neck before healing, it is execution; and if he slit after healing, then it is upon this dispute, that is the correct [view]. And fingers, even if they are subordinate in standing (qiyaman) to the palm, so the palm is subordinate to them in purpose, contrary to the limb, because it is subordinate to the life in every respect.' Translation: And when the guardian cut the hand then slit his neck before healing, then it is execution; and if he slit after healing, then it is upon this dispute. This is correct. And fingers, in terms of standing and function, even if they are subordinate to the palm, so the palm is subordinate to them in purpose, contrary to the limb, because these (limbs) are subordinate to the life in every respect. Explanation: Imam says: Similarly, O Sahibayn, your inference from the fourth instance is also not absolutely correct, because it requires detail. If the guardian, after cutting the hand, slit his neck before recovery, then here blood money would not be obligatory, because the guardian has received his right. But if he slit after healing, then Imam says the same here too, that blood money would be obligatory, so inference from this is not correct. And also the fifth instance that you presented as an example in istishhad, inference from that is also not correct, because in one respect fingers are subordinate to the palm, and in another respect the palm is subordinate to the fingers. The first subordination is because without the palm, fingers cannot stand, and the palm is subordinate because without the palm, nothing can be grasped with the fingers.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the liability (diyat) when the guardian (wali) of a murder victim cuts off the hand of the murderer before execution of qisas. The passage begins by stating the ruling: if the wound from the cut causes death (saraya, i.e., spreads and kills), then the guardian has received his right (qisas) and is not liable for anything. However, if the wound heals, then the guardian must pay diyat (blood money) for the hand. This is because the guardian's right was to take the life (qisas), but by cutting the hand he acted outside his right. A shubha (doubt) arises due to his right to kill, so instead of qisas (which would be required by pure qiyas), wealth (diyat) becomes obligatory due to the shubha. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is then elaborated: ownership (milk) of qisas is a necessary (daruri) ownership that only becomes manifest upon actual execution (istifa'), forgiveness ('afw), or taking compensation (i'wad). Before that, it is not manifest because necessity is measured by its extent. The criminal is a free and inviolable person; the guardian's ownership of his life is granted only out of necessity (for retaliation). Therefore, this ownership is limited to the three modes of exercising it. If the guardian cuts off a limb without exercising any of these three, he has acted without right and must compensate. The commentary then addresses the Sahibayn's istishhad (objection by example). The Sahibayn had presented several instances to support their view that the guardian should not be liable. Imam Abu Hanifa responds to each. Third instance: If the guardian does not forgive and the wound does not spread, the Sahibayn claim no diyat is due. Imam responds that the lack of spread does not prove the cut was with right; the wound may still kill later. Only upon complete healing (bar') does it become clear that the cut was without right, because the right of qisas is only over the life, not the limb. Therefore, diyat is not due immediately but becomes due if the wound heals. If it kills, then the guardian's act becomes istifa' (execution). Fourth instance: If the guardian cuts the hand then slits the neck before healing, it is istifa' (no diyat). If after healing, it is on the same dispute (Imam holds diyat wajib). Fifth instance: Regarding fingers and palm being subordinate to each other in different respects (standing vs. purpose), the Sahibayn's analogy is rejected because limbs (atraf) are subordinate to life in every respect, unlike fingers to palm. Throughout, Imam Abu Hanifa insists that the guardian's ownership of qisas is strictly limited to the life, and any action on limbs without proper execution or forgiveness incurs diyat unless the wound causes death (making it retroactively an execution). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
سرایت (sarāyat): The spreading of a wound or injury through the body, ultimately causing death.
ملک قصاص (milk al-qiṣāṣ): The legal ownership or right of the victim's guardian to demand retaliation (qisas) against the murderer.
استیفاء (istīfāʾ): The actual execution of qisas, i.e., taking the life of the murderer.
دیت (diyat): Blood money; compensation paid for homicide or bodily harm.
شبہ (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity regarding the legal status of an act, often mitigating punishment or converting qisas to diyat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the wali cuts off the murderer's hand and the wound heals completely, what is the ruling?
A) The wali must pay diyat for the hand.
B) The wali is not liable because the wali had a right to the life.
C) The wali must be executed for murder.
D) The wali is exempt regardless of healing.

Key Takeaway
The wali's ownership of qisas is a necessary right limited to the life; any act on a limb without proper execution, forgiveness, or compensation incurs diyat unless the wound causes death.

Qisas — Retaliation
advanced
8 min
Liability for Diyat When Limb Qisas Causes Death
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyat liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-school dispute on diyat liability when limb qisas causes death, and apply Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning to distinguish the Sahibayn's analogies.

Core Idea
Executing qisas on a limb does not license death; unintended spread triggers separate diyat liability.

This passage from Ashraf al-Bidaya presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on a nuanced issue in jinayat: when a person lawfully executes qisas on a limb (e.g., cutting a hand) and the wound spreads to cause the criminal's death, is the executor liable for diyat an-nafs (full blood money)? The Sahibayn argue no, based on the principle that executing a lawful right cannot be made conditional on safety, while Imam Abu Hanifa holds the executor liable because the right was only to the limb, and death is a separate harm. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in analyzing qiyas and distinguishing subordinate from principal in legal causation.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the core scenario: a person (victim) has the right to qisas on a limb (e.g., hand) of the criminal. He cuts the hand, but the wound spreads and the criminal dies. State the two rulings: Imam Abu Hanifa says the executor is liable for diyat an-nafs; the Sahibayn say he is not liable.
The dispute is about whether the executor is responsible for the death when he only had the right to the limb.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof and analogies
The Sahibayn argue that since the executor lawfully exercised his right (cutting), there is no transgression. They analogize to the imam, lancet-operator, cupper, and one ordered to cut a hand—none are liable when their lawful acts cause death. They also argue that imposing a condition of safety would close the door of qisas because spread is beyond the executor's control.
The Sahibayn use four sub-examples (istishhad) to support their view; the passage discusses the third, fourth, and fifth.
3
Follow Imam Abu Hanifa's refutation of each sub-example
Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes each: (3) The third sub-example (wound does not spread but not healed) does not prove non-liability because the wound has not yet healed—healing is the benchmark for 'cutting without right.' (4) The fourth sub-example (cutting neck before vs. after healing) is detailed: before healing is execution of right, after healing is a new act where liability arises. (5) The fingers-palm example actually supports Imam Abu Hanifa: cutting the hand (subordinate to the soul) does not obtain the soul, just as cutting fingers does not obtain the palm in all respects.
The commentator declares Imam Abu Hanifa's position as 'sahih' (correct).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practically: if the hand-cutter dies from wound spread, according to Imam Abu Hanifa the executor pays full diyah (100 camels); according to Sahibayn, no payment. The commentator prefers Imam Abu Hanifa's view, making it the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school.
This ruling is from al-Mabsut (Zahir al-Riwayah), not from al-Hidayah itself.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ ترجمہ اور بہر حال جب کہ اس نے معاف نہیں کیا اور نہ زخم نے سرایت کی تو ہم کہیں گے کہ اس قطع کا بغیر حق کے قطع ہونا برأت س ظاہر ہو گا یہاں تک کہ اگر ولی نے ہاتھ کاٹا اور معاف نہیں کیا اور اچھا ہو گیا تو صحیح یہ ہے کہ صورت اختلافی ہے۔ تشریح یہاں سے امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ اے صاحبین ہم نےچار جزئیات استشہاد میں پیش کی ہیں تو ان میں سے تیسری جزئی سے آپ کا استشہاد درست نہیں تیسری جزئی یہ تھی کہ نہ ولی نے معاف کیا اور نہ زخم نے سرایت کی تو یہاں دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ بات صحیح ہے مگر اس سے آپ کا استدلال درست نہیں اس لئے کہ سرایت نہ کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ابھی زخم کی پوزیشن کیا رخ اختیار کرنے والی ہے اس کا کچھ پتہ نہیں چلا مگر ابھی زخم اچھا تو نہیں ہوا۔
جب زخم ابھی اچھا نہیں ہوا تو احتمال ہے کہ مجرم اس زخم کی وجہ سے مرجائے تو پھر ولی پر ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ ناحق قطع اس وقت کہلاتا ہے کہ زخم اچھا ہو گیا ہوتا اور یہاں تو اچھا نہیں ہوا البتہ ابھی اس نے سرایت نہیں کی تو احتمال تو ہے کہ سرایت کر جائے اس وجہ سے ابھی دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ لہذا اس جزئی استدلال درست نہیں رہا۔ ور نہ اگر ولی مجرم کا ہاتھ کاٹ دے اور اس نے معاف بھی نہ کیا ہو اور زخم اچھا ہو گیا ہو تو امام صاحب یہاں بھی دیت کو واجب
کرتے ہیں۔
خلاصہ کلام تیسری جزئی سے استدلال ٹھیک نہیں ہے۔
چوتھے استشہاد کا جواب
واذا قطع ثم حز رقبته قبل البرء فهو استيفاء ولو حز بعد البرء فهو على هذا الخلاف هو الصحيح و صابع وان كانت تابعة قياما بالكف فالكف تابعة لها غرضا بخلاف الطرف لانها تابعة للنفس من كل وجه . ترجمہ اور جب کہ ولی نے ہاتھ کاٹا ہو پھر اچھا ہونے سے پہلے اس کی گردن کاٹ دی ہو تو یہ استیفاء ہے اور اگر اچھا ہونے کے بعد کائی ہو تو یہ اس اختلاف پر ہے یہی صحیح ہے اور انگلیاں قیام و تحصل کے اعتبار سے اگر چہ ہتھیلی کا تابع ہیں پس ہتھیلی انگلیوں کے تابع ہے۔ غرض کے لحاظ سے بخلاف طرف کے اس لئے کہ یہ (اطراف ) ہر اعتبار سے نفس کے تابع ہیں۔ تشریح امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں اسی طرح اے صاحبین آپ کا چوتھی جزئی سے مطلقاً استدلال بھی سیج نہیں کیونکہ وہ تفصیل طلب ہے اگر ولی نے ہاتھ کاٹنے کے بعد تندرستی سے پہلے ہی اس کی گردن کاٹ دی ہو تو یہاں دیت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ ولی نے اپنا حق
وصول کیا ہے۔ لیکن اگر اچھا ہونے کے بعد گردن کائی ہو تو امام صاحب یہاں بھی وہی فرماتے ہیں کہ دیت واجب ہوگی لہذا اس سے استدلال
درست نہ ہوگا۔
اور اسے صاحبین تم نے جو پانچویں جزئی استشہاد میں مثال دیتے ہوئے پیش کی تھی اس سے بھی استدلال صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک اعتبار سے انگلیاں ہتھیلی کے تابع ہیں اور ایک اعتبار سے ہتھیلی انگلیوں کے تابع ہے، اول کی تبعیت اس وجہ سے ہے کہ
بغیر ہتھیلی کے انگلیوں کا قیام نہ ہوگا اور ہتھیلی اس لئے تابع ہے کہ ہتھیلی کے بغیر انگلیوں سے پکڑا نہیں جائے گا۔

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ جب ایک اعتبار سے اصابع متنوع ٹھہریں تو اصابع کے کاٹنے سے حق حاصل ہو جائے گا لیکن ہاتھ کے کاٹنے سے قصاص نفس حاصل نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ ہاتھ تو ہر اعتبار سے نفس کے تابع ہے اور تابع کی تحصیل مبتوع کی تحصیل نہیں ہوتی البتہ متبوع کی تحصیل تابع کی تحصیل ہو جائے گی۔
ایک شخص کو قاطع ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حق تھا اور اس نے ہاتھ کاٹ دیا پھر کئے ہوئے ہاتھ کا زہر پورے بدن میں سرایت کر گیا بالآخر وہ شخص مر گیا تو ہاتھ کاٹنے والا ضامن ہوگا یا نہیں .... اقوال فقہاء
قال ومن له القصاص فى الطرف اذا استوفاه ثم سرى الى النفس ومات يضمن دية النفس عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يضمن لانه استوفى حقه وهو القطع ولا يمكن التقييد بوصف السلامة لمافيه من سد باب القصاص اذا الاعترض عن السراية ليس في وسعه فصار كالامام والبزاغ والحجام والمامور بقطع اليد ترجمہ محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا اور جس کے لئے طرف میں قصاص ہو جب کہ اس نے اس کو وصول کر لیا پھر زخم نفس کی جانب سے سرایت کر گیا اور وہ مر گیا تو وہ (من له القصاص فی الطرف ( ضامن ہو گا نفس کی دیت کا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور فرمایا صاحبین نے ضامن نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس نے (من له القصاص نے ) اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے اور وہ حق قطع ہے اور سلامتی کی صفت کے ساتھ مقید کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے کہ تقید میں قصاص کے دروازہ کو بند کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ سرایت سے احتراز اس کے بس میں نہیں ہے تو امام کے مثل اور نشتر گانے والے اور حجام کے مثل ہو گیا اور اس کے مثل ہو گیا جس کو قطع ید کا حکم دے دیا گیا ہو۔ تشریح یہ مسئلہ ہدایہ میں مذکور نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ عبارت مبسوط کی ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زید نے بکر کا ہاتھ عمدا کاٹ لیا جس کی وجہ سے زید پر ہاتھ کا قصاص واجب ہو گیا۔ اب بکر نے قصاص میں اس کا ہاتھ کا نا لیکن زید کا یہ زخم سرایت کر گیا جس سے زید مرگیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک بکر پردیت واجب ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دیت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بکر نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے اور اس حق کو وصول کرنا اس کیلئے جائز ہے تو بکر کی طرف سے کچھ تعدی نہیں پائی گئی۔ اب رہی یہ بات کہ بکر کا حق تو صرف کا نا تھا اور یہاں یہ مر گیا ہے۔ تو صاحبین نے اس کا جواب یہ دیا ہے کہ یہاں یہ قید لگانا کہ زید صحیح سالم رہے اور ہاتھ کاٹنے سے نہ مرے یہ ایسی قید ہے جس سے قصاص کا دروازہ ہی بند ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یہ بات بکر کے بس میں ہی نہیں لہذا اس کا مکلف بنانا بھی ممکن نہ ہوگا اور اسکی نظیر یہ چار جزئیات ہیں۔
(1) امام یا اس کے نائب نے کسی مجرم کا ہاتھ کاٹا اور زخم سرایت کر گیا اور مجرم مر گیا تو امام پر کوئی مضمان نہ ہوگا۔ (۲ نشتر لگانے والے نے نشتر لگایا جس کی وجہ سے زخم سرایت کر گیا اور آدمی مر گیا تو اس پر نعمان نہ ہو گا۔
Book of Crimes. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 15. Translation: And in any case, when he did not forgive and the wound did not spread, we will say that this cutting without right becomes apparent as immunity, until if the guardian cut off the hand and did not forgive and it healed, then the correct view is that the case is disputed. Explanation: Here Imam Sahib says: O Sahibayn, we presented four sub-issues in istishhad; among them, your istishhad from the third sub-issue is not correct. The third sub-issue was: the guardian did not forgive and the wound did not spread, so here diyah is not obligatory. That is correct, but your deduction from it is not correct because the meaning of 'not spreading' is that the direction the wound will take is not yet known; the wound has not yet healed. When the wound has not healed, there is a possibility that the criminal may die from this wound, then there would be no guarantee on the guardian. Summary: Unjust cutting is when the wound has healed, but here it has not healed; however it has not spread, so there is possibility of spreading, therefore diyah is not yet obligatory. Hence this sub-issue's deduction is not valid. Otherwise, if the guardian cuts the criminal's hand and he has not forgiven and the wound has healed, then Imam Sahib makes diyah obligatory here as well. Summary: The deduction from the third sub-issue is not correct. Answer to the fourth istishhad: 'And if he cuts then cuts his neck before healing, then it is istifa'; and if he cuts after healing, then it is upon this difference; that is correct. And fingers, even though they are subordinate to the palm in terms of establishment and grasping, so the palm is subordinate to them in purpose, unlike the limb because the limb is subordinate to the soul in every respect.' Translation: And when the guardian cuts the hand then cuts his neck before healing, then this is istifa' (execution of right). And if after healing, then it is upon this difference; this is correct. And fingers, in terms of establishment and grasping, are subordinate to the palm; so the palm is subordinate to them in purpose, unlike the limb because limbs are subordinate to the soul in every respect. Explanation: Imam Sahib says: Similarly, O Sahibayn, your deduction from the fourth sub-issue absolutely is also not correct because it requires detail. If after cutting the hand, the guardian cuts his neck before recovery, then diyah is not obligatory because the guardian has received his right. But if after healing he cuts the neck, then Imam Sahib says the same: diyah will be obligatory; hence deduction from it is not correct. And the fifth sub-issue which you Sahibayn presented as an example, deduction from it is also not correct. Because from one aspect fingers are subordinate to the palm and from another aspect the palm is subordinate to fingers; the first subordination is because without the palm, fingers cannot be established; and the palm is subordinate because without the palm, one cannot grasp with fingers. When from one aspect the fingers are diverse, then cutting the fingers will obtain the right, but cutting the hand will not obtain qisas for the soul because the hand is subordinate to the soul in every respect, and obtaining the subordinate does not obtain the principal, but obtaining the principal obtains the subordinate. There was a person who had the right to cut the hand of the cutter; he cut the hand, then the poison from the cut hand spread throughout the body and eventually that person died; then is the hand-cutter liable or not? Statements of the jurists. He (Muhammad) said in Mabsut: And whoever has qisas in the limb, when he executes it then it spreads to the soul and he dies, he is liable for the diyah of the soul according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is not liable because he executed his right, which is the cutting, and it is not possible to restrict it with the condition of safety because that would close the door of qisas, since avoidance of spread is not within his power. So he becomes like the imam, the lancet-operator, the cupper, and the one ordered to cut off the hand. Translation: Muhammad said in Mabsut: And whoever has qisas in the limb, when he executes it then the wound spreads to the soul and he dies, he is liable for the diyah of the soul according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: He is not liable because he executed his right, and that right is the cutting, and it is not possible to restrict it with the condition of safety because that would close the door of qisas, since avoidance of spread is not within his power. So he becomes like the imam, the lancet-operator, the cupper, and the one ordered to cut off the hand. Explanation: This issue is not mentioned in Hidayah; rather this text is from Mabsut. The issue is: Zayd cut Bakr's hand intentionally, which made qisas on the hand obligatory upon Zayd. Then Bakr cut his hand in qisas, but Zayd's wound spread and he died. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, Bakr is liable for diyah; according to the Sahibayn, diyah is not obligatory. The Sahibayn's proof is that Bakr executed his right, and executing that right is permissible for him, so there is no transgression from Bakr. As for the matter that Bakr's right was only to cut, and here the person died, the Sahibayn respond by saying that imposing the condition that Zayd remain safe and not die from the cutting is a condition that would close the door of qisas entirely, because it is not within Bakr's power; hence it is not possible to obligate him. And their analogy is these four sub-issues: (1) The imam or his deputy cuts a criminal's hand and the wound spreads and the criminal dies; the imam is not liable. (2) The lancet-operator applied a lancet which caused the wound to spread and the person died; he is not liable.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Bidaya, a commentary on al-Hidayah, addresses a key dispute in the Hanafi school regarding the liability for diyah when a person executes qisas on a limb and the wound subsequently spreads, causing death. The passage is a response to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) who had argued using four sub-examples to support their view that no diyah is due. Imam Abu Hanifa's position, supported by the commentator, is that diyah is obligatory. The commentator systematically dismantles the Sahibayn's examples. The third sub-example (where the wound does not spread and is not yet healed) is rejected because the wound's outcome is unknown; the diyah is not yet due because the wound hasn't healed, not because no harm was done. The fourth example (cutting the neck before vs. after healing) is distinguished: before healing, it is execution of the right; after healing, it is a separate act, and Imam Abu Hanifa holds diyah due. The fifth example about fingers and palm shows that subordinate status matters: cutting fingers fulfills the right for the hand, but cutting the hand does not fulfill qisas for the soul because the hand is subordinate to the soul in every respect. The core ruling from Imam Muhammad's al-Mabsut is then quoted: The one who has qisas on a limb and executes it, then the wound spreads and kills, is liable for the diyah of the soul according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn disagree, arguing that the execution of a lawful right cannot be made conditional on safety, as that would block qisas entirely. They analogize to the imam, the lancet-operator, the cupper, and the one ordered to cut a hand—none are liable. The commentator notes that this issue is not in al-Hidayah but in al-Mabsut, indicating it is from the Zahir al-Riwayah. The student should note that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as it is given preference by the commentator.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional bodily harm or murder; the right of the victim or guardian to inflict equivalent harm on the perpetrator.
دية (diyah): Blood money or financial compensation paid to the victim's heirs for homicide or bodily injury.
سرایت (sarāyat): The spreading of a wound or injury from the initial site to other parts of the body, often causing additional harm or death.
استیفاء (istifa'): Execution of a right; taking full and lawful possession of what is due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if a person executes qisas on a hand and the wound spreads causing the criminal's death, what is the ruling?
A) The executor is not liable because he executed a lawful right.
B) The executor is liable for the diyah of the hand only.
C) The executor is liable for diyat an-nafs (full blood money).
D) The executor is not liable because the spread was beyond his control.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, executing qisas on a limb does not grant immunity for subsequent death from wound spread; the executor is liable for full diyah according to the relied-upon position of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Qisas — Retaliation
advanced
10 min
Liability for Qisas of Limb When Wound Spreads to Soul
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for diyat when qisas for a limb causes death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding liability for diyat when qisas for a limb leads to death, and explain the key usul principles underlying each view.

Core Idea
Executing qisas for a limb does not grant immunity for unintended killing; the dispute hinges on commission and the condition of safety.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute from al-Mabsut. When a person entitled to qisas for a limb cuts off the offender's hand, but the wound spreads and causes death, is the executor liable for diyat? Imam Abu Hanifa holds liability, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold no liability. Understanding their different usul principles—particularly the roles of commission, safety conditions, and doubt—clarifies how Hanafi jurists balance rights with unintended consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the parties
The issue: Is the executor of qisas for a limb liable for diyat if the wound spreads and causes death? The parties: Imam Abu Hanifa holds liability; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold no liability.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa: The executor must pay diyat al-nafs (blood money for the soul). Sahibayn: No diyat is owed.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that the executor exacted his legitimate right to cut, and cannot be held liable for the spread because it is beyond his control. Restricting the act by a condition of safety would close the door of qisas. They analogize to the imam, scarifier, cupper, and doctor, who are not liable for death resulting from their permitted acts.
These analogies are central to their argument.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the executor killed without right, because his right was limited to cutting, not killing. The wound is one that typically leads to death, so the act is considered killing. Qisas for killing is dropped due to doubt (shubha), but financial compensation remains. He distinguishes the analogies: in those cases, the actor is commissioned either by shari'ah (imam) or by contract (doctor), and commissioned acts are not conditioned on safety. Here, the executor acts on his own right, and the victim is encouraged to pardon, so the executor is like a hunter liable for unintended consequences.
The key distinction is the nature of commission.
5
Identify the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the executor pays diyat; under Sahibayn, he pays nothing. This affects the financial responsibility of the person executing qisas.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

لانه استوفى حقه وهو القطع ولا يمكن التقييد بوصف السلامة لمافيه من سد باب القصاص اذا الاعترض عن السراية ليس في وسعه فصار كالامام والبزاغ والحجام والمامور بقطع اليد ترجمہ محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا اور جس کے لئے طرف میں قصاص ہو جب کہ اس نے اس کو وصول کر لیا پھر زخم نفس کی جانب سے سرایت کر گیا اور وہ مر گیا تو وہ (من له القصاص فی الطرف ( ضامن ہو گا نفس کی دیت کا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور فرمایا صاحبین نے ضامن نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس نے (من له القصاص نے ) اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے اور وہ حق قطع ہے اور سلامتی کی صفت کے ساتھ مقید کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے اس وجہ سے کہ تقید میں قصاص کے دروازہ کو بند کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ سرایت سے احتراز اس کے بس میں نہیں ہے تو امام کے مثل اور نشتر گانے والے اور حجام کے مثل ہو گیا اور اس کے مثل ہو گیا جس کو قطع ید کا حکم دے دیا گیا ہو۔ تشریح یہ مسئلہ ہدایہ میں مذکور نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ عبارت مبسوط کی ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زید نے بکر کا ہاتھ عمدا کاٹ لیا جس کی وجہ سے زید پر ہاتھ کا قصاص واجب ہو گیا۔ اب بکر نے قصاص میں اس کا ہاتھ کا نا لیکن زید کا یہ زخم سرایت کر گیا جس سے زید مرگیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک بکر پردیت واجب ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دیت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بکر نے اپنا حق وصول کیا ہے اور اس حق کو وصول کرنا اس کیلئے جائز ہے تو بکر کی طرف سے کچھ تعدی نہیں پائی گئی۔ اب رہی یہ بات کہ بکر کا حق تو صرف کا نا تھا اور یہاں یہ مر گیا ہے۔ تو صاحبین نے اس کا جواب یہ دیا ہے کہ یہاں یہ قید لگانا کہ زید صحیح سالم رہے اور ہاتھ کاٹنے سے نہ مرے یہ ایسی قید ہے جس سے قصاص کا دروازہ ہی بند ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یہ بات بکر کے بس میں ہی نہیں لہذا اس کا مکلف بنانا بھی ممکن نہ ہوگا اور اسکی نظیر یہ چار جزئیات ہیں۔ (1) امام یا اس کے نائب نے کسی مجرم کا ہاتھ کاٹا اور زخم سرایت کر گیا اور مجرم مر گیا تو امام پر کوئی مضمان نہ ہوگا۔ (۲ نشتر لگانے والے نے نشتر لگایا جس کی وجہ سے زخم سرایت کر گیا اور آدمی مر گیا تو اس پر نعمان نہ ہو گا۔ كتاب الجنايات الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ سنگی (پچھنے لگانے والے نے سنگی لگائی جس سے آدمی مر گیا تو حجام پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ کسی مریض نے ڈاکٹر سے کہا کہ میرے ہاتھ کا آپریشن کر دے اس نے آپریشن کیا جس سے مریض مر گیا تو ڈاکٹر پر کوئی ضمان نہ ہوگا۔ تو جیسے ان تمام صورتوں میں ضمان نہیں آتا ایسے ہی صورت مذکورہ میں بھی منمان نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ه انه قتل بغير حق لان حقه فى القطع وهذا وقع قتلا ولهذا لو وقع ظلما كان قتلا ولانه جرح افضى الى ات الحيوة في مجرى العادة وهو مسمى القتل الا ان القصاص سقط للشبهة فوجب المال بخارات ما شهد ابه من المسائل لانه مكلف فيها بالفعل اما تقلد اكا لامام او عقدا كما في غيره منها والواجبات کہتے ہیں ) مگر شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص تو ساقط ہو گیا تو مال واجب ہو گا بخلاف ان مسائل کے جن سے صاحبین نے نہاد کیا ہے اس لئے کہ فاعل ان میں فعل کا مکلف ہے یا تو بر بناء خلافت و حکومت جیسے امام یا بر بناء دیت اس پر واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص ظلما کسی کا ہاتھ کاٹ دے اور وہ زخم سرایت کر جائے تو اب یہ قطع نہیں بلکہ قتل کہلاتا ہے اور اس پر احکام قتل جاری تے ہیں۔ اور زخم سے آدمی کا مر جانا خلاف عادت مقید نہیں ۔ ڈاکہ
Book of Crimes. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume 15. When from one perspective the fingers are diverse, then from cutting the fingers the right is obtained, but from cutting the hand the qisas of the soul is not obtained because the hand is in every respect subordinate to the soul, and obtaining the subordinate does not constitute obtaining the superior; rather, obtaining the superior constitutes obtaining the subordinate. A person had the right to cut the hand of the cutter, and he cut off the hand, then the venom from the cut hand spread throughout the body, and eventually that person died: will the one who cut the hand be liable or not? ... Statements of the jurists: He said: "Whosoever has qisas for a limb, when he executes it and then it spreads to the soul and he dies, he will be liable for the blood money of the soul according to Abu Hanifa. But they (the two companions) said: He will not be liable because he has exacted his right, which is the cutting, and it is not possible to restrict it with the condition of safety because that would close the door of qisas, since guarding against spreading is not in his power. So he is like the imam, the scarifier, the cupper, and the one ordered to cut off a hand." Translation: Muhammad said in al-Mabsut: And the one for whom there is qisas in a limb, when he exacts it then the wound spreads to the soul and he dies, then he (the one with qisas for the limb) will be liable for the blood money of the soul according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two companions said he will not be liable because he (the one with qisas) has exacted his right, and that right is cutting, and it is not possible to restrict it with the attribute of safety because in that restriction there is closure of the door of qisas, since guarding against spreading is not in his power. So he becomes like the imam, the scarifier, the cupper, and the one who is ordered to cut off a hand. Explanation: This issue is not mentioned in Hidaya; rather, this text is from al-Mabsut. The issue is that Zayd intentionally cut off Bakr's hand, thereby making qisas of the hand obligatory upon Zayd. Now Bakr cuts off his hand in qisas, but this wound of Zayd spreads and Zayd dies. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, diyah is obligatory upon Bakr. According to the two companions, diyah is not obligatory. The proof of the two companions is that Bakr has exacted his right, and exacting that right is permissible for him; thus no transgression is found on Bakr's part. As for the matter that Bakr's right was only cutting, and here he died, the two companions responded that imposing the condition that Zayd remain safe and not die from the cutting is a condition that would close the door of qisas altogether, because this matter is not within Bakr's power. Therefore, making him responsible for it is not possible. And their analogies are these four cases: (1) The imam or his deputy cuts off a criminal's hand and the wound spreads and the criminal dies; no liability on the imam. (2) The scarifier makes an incision and the wound spreads and the person dies; no liability on him. (3) The cupper applies cupping and the person dies; no liability on the cupper. (4) A patient tells a doctor to operate on his hand; he operates and the patient dies; no liability on the doctor. So just as in all these cases liability does not arise, similarly in the mentioned case liability will not arise. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: It is that he killed without right, because his right is in cutting, and this occurred as killing. Hence, if it had occurred wrongfully, it would be killing. And because it is a wound that usually leads to the loss of life, and that is called killing. However, qisas is dropped due to the doubt, so financial compensation becomes obligatory. Contrary to the cases cited by the two companions, because in those cases the doer is either mandated by khilafah and governance like the imam, or by a contract of hire like the others, and obligations are not characterized by safety, like shooting an arrow at an enemy. In our case, there is neither obligation nor commitment, because the person is encouraged to pardon unconditionally, so it resembles hunting. And this is the proof of Imam Sahib: Since the right-holder's right was cutting, and he killed him, he did this without right; therefore he is liable and diyah is obligatory upon him. Because if someone wrongfully cuts off another's hand and the wound spreads, this is not called cutting but killing, and the rulings of killing apply to it. And a person dying from a wound is not contrary to habit; rather, it happens that a severe wound causes death, and a wound from which one usually dies is called killing. Therefore, the ruling of killing applies. Rather, in this case qisas would be obligatory, but due to the doubt, qisas is dropped, so financial compensation becomes obligatory. And the proof from the specific cases cited by the two companions is not correct, because in all those cases the cutter is commissioned, and in the act of the commissioned agent safety is not necessary. Among these, the first is commissioned by virtue of shari'ah because he is the ruler, and the last three are commissioned by virtue of a contract of hire. And where a person is commissioned, his act is not restricted by the attribute of safety.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding liability when a person entitled to qisas for a limb (e.g., cutting off a hand) executes the qisas, but the wound then spreads (sari) and causes the death of the offender. The question is whether the executor of qisas is liable for diyat (blood money) for the soul. The dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The text is from al-Mabsut, not from al-Hidayah, as noted by the commentator. The scenario: Zayd intentionally cuts off Bakr's hand, making qisas of the hand obligatory upon Zayd. Bakr then executes qisas by cutting Zayd's hand, but the wound spreads and Zayd dies. According to Abu Hanifa, Bakr is liable for diyat al-nafs (blood money for the soul). According to the two companions, Bakr is not liable. The Sahibayn's argument: Bakr executed his legitimate right; he did not transgress. He cannot be held responsible for the spread because it is beyond his control. They draw analogy to four cases where no liability arises: (1) the imam or his deputy executing a prescribed amputation; (2) a scarifier (one who makes incisions for medical purposes); (3) a cupper (one who performs cupping); (4) a doctor performing a requested operation. In all these, the actor is either acting under authority (imam) or under a contract (hire), and safety is not a condition. Imam Abu Hanifa's argument: Bakr killed without right because his right was only to cut, not to kill. The act here resulted in killing (since it is a wound that typically leads to death). Therefore, it is considered killing. Qisas for killing would normally apply, but it is dropped due to the doubt (whether it was intentional killing or accidental in the course of qisas), so financial compensation (diyah) is due. Abu Hanifa distinguishes the analogous cases: in those, the actor is either commissioned by shari'ah (imam) or by contract (doctor, etc.), and such commissioned acts are not conditioned on safety. In Bakr's case, there is no such commission; he is merely exercising his personal right to qisas. Moreover, a person is encouraged to pardon (afw), so unconditionally he is like a hunter who kills game – he is liable for the unintended consequences. Thus, Abu Hanifa holds Bakr liable for diyat.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment by inflicting the same injury as the victim suffered; here specifically the right to cut off the hand of the offender.
سرایت (sarāyat): The spread or extension of a wound or infection from the original site to the rest of the body, leading to death.
دیت (diyat): Financial compensation (blood money) paid to the victim's heirs for bodily harm or homicide.
تابع (tābi‘): Subordinate; the hand is described as tābi‘ (subordinate) to the soul (nafs), meaning ruling on the hand does not cover the soul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the executor of qisas for a limb liable for diyat when the wound spreads and causes death?
A) Because the executor intended to kill the offender.
B) Because the executor's right was only to cut, and the resulting killing is without right, so compensation is due.
C) Because the executor is commissioned by the state.
D) Because the wound is not a typical cause of death.

Key Takeaway
The liability for unintended consequences of qisas depends on whether the executor is considered commissioned or acting on his own right, and whether safety conditions are implied.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Qisas as Khilafa: Imam Abu Hanifa's Proof
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof that qisas is a khilafa (substitution) not inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Imam Abu Hanifa's proof that qisas is a khilafa (substitution) not inheritance, and identify the procedural consequence for representation of heirs.

Core Idea
Qisas is a fresh right for heirs (khilafa), not inherited property — each heir must claim individually.

This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's rational proof (dalil aqli) that the right to qisas (retaliation) passes to the victim's heirs as a substitution (khilafa) rather than through inheritance. The distinction has a direct procedural implication: a present heir cannot represent an absent heir in court, requiring the absent heir to present evidence separately. We will unpack the proof, focusing on the analogy with property ownership after death.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa claims about qisas: that it is a khilafa (substitution) for the heirs, not an inheritance (waratha).
This is the foundation of the procedural rule that follows.
2
Identify the rational proof
Find the analogy (qiyas) used: a person sets a net, and game is caught after his death; he owns the game. This shows that a deceased can own property after death.
The analouge (asl) is property ownership; the far' is qisas.
3
Analyze the illa
The effective cause is that ownership after death is possible for property (amwal) but not for acts (af‘al). Qisas is an act, not property.
Because the deceased lacks capacity to perform acts, qisas cannot be owned by him; thus it is a fresh right for heirs.
4
Derive the procedural rule
Since qisas is a khilafa, each heir has an independent right. Therefore, one heir cannot act as a litigant (khasm) for another absent heir.
The absent heir must appear and present his own evidence to claim his share of qisas.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
If qisas were inherited, a present heir could represent all heirs. Because it is khilafa, representation is not allowed, affecting court procedure.
This distinguishes qisas from diya (blood money), which is inherited and allows representation.

وله ان القصاص طريقه طريق الخلافة دون الوراثة الاترى ان ملك القصاص يثبت بعد المو والميت ليس من اهله بخلاف الدين والدية لإنه من اهل الملك فى الاموال كما اذا نصب شب وتعقل بها صيد بعد موته فانه يملكه واذا كان طريقه الاثبات ابتداء لا ينتصب احدهم خصما الباقين فيعيد البيئة بعد حضوره
ترجمہ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قصاص اس کا طریقہ طریق خلافت ہے نہ کہ وراثت کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ ملک قصاص مو کے بعد ثابت ہوتی ہے اور میت ملک قصاص کا اہل نہیں ہے بخلاف دین اور دیت کے اس لئے کہ میت اموال میں اہل ملک میں سے جیسے کسی نے شکار کے لئے جال لگایا اور اس کی موت کے بعد اس میں شکار پھنسا تو میت اس شکار کا الگ ہو جائے گا اور جب کہ قصاص طریق ابتداء ( ورثا کے لئے ) اثبات ہے تو ان میں سے کوئی باقیوں کی طرف سے خصم نہ ہوگا تو غائب اپنے حاضر ہونے کے بعد بہ اعادہ کرے گا۔
تشریح یہ امام صاحب کی دلیل ہے کہ قصاص خلافت ہے وراثت نہیں اور خلافت کا اصول یہ ہے کہ اس میں ایک وارث دیگر و کی طرف سے خصم نہیں ہو سکتا ۔ لہذا پھر ساجد کو حاضر ہونے کے بعد بینہ کا اعادہ کرنا پڑے گا۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ملک قصاص ملک اموال نہیں بلکہ ملک فعل ہے اور میست اس کا تو اہل ہے کہ وہ اموال کا مالک بنے اور اس اہل نہیں کہ وہ افعال کا مالک بنے۔ لہذا ملک قصاص ایسا فعل ہے جس کا ثبوت موت کے بعد ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے میت اس کا اہل نہیں ہوگا کہ وہ قصاص کا مالک۔
البتہ دین اور دیت چونکہ مال ہیں اس وجہ سے میت ان کا مالک ہو گا اور ان میں وارث کی ملکیت بطریق وراثت ہوگی۔ اور میت اموال کا مالک ہو سکتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر بکر نے شکار کے لئے جال لگایا تھا اور اس کے مرنے کے بعد جال : شکار پھنسا ہے تو بکر اس شکار کا مالک ہوگا۔
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: He said: The way of qisas is the way of khilafa (substitution), not inheritance. Do you not see that ownership of qisas is established after death, and the deceased is not eligible for it, unlike debt and blood-money (diya), because the deceased is among those eligible for ownership of property? Just as if someone sets a net and game becomes caught in it after his death, then he owns it. And since its method of establishment is initially (for the heirs), none of them can stand as a litigant for the rest, so the absent one will repeat the proof after his presence. Translation: And Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the way of qisas is the way of substitution, not inheritance. Do you not see that ownership of qisas is established after death, and the deceased is not eligible for ownership of qisas, unlike debt and blood-money, because the deceased is among the eligible for ownership of property. For example, if someone sets a net for hunting and after his death game is caught in it, then the deceased will own that game. And when qisas is established initially (for the heirs), none of them can be a litigant for the others, so the absent one, after his presence, will repeat the proof. Commentary: This is Imam's proof that qisas is substitution, not inheritance. The principle of substitution is that in it, one heir cannot be a litigant for another. Therefore, Sajid (absent heir), after presence, will have to repeat the proof. The reason is that ownership of qisas is not ownership of property, but ownership of an act. The deceased is only eligible to own property, not acts. Therefore, qisas is an act established after death, so the deceased is not eligible to own it. However, debt and blood-money, since they are property, the deceased owns them, and the heirs' ownership is through inheritance. And the deceased can own property, as evidenced by the example: if someone set a net for hunting and after his death game is caught in it, the deceased owns that game.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's proof that the right to qisas (retaliation) passes to the heirs as a khilafa (substitution) rather than through inheritance (waratha). The distinction is crucial for procedural rules: if qisas were inherited, a present heir could represent an absent one in court. Since it is a khilafa, each heir must establish their own right individually. The imam uses a rational analogy: a deceased person can own property (like game caught in his net) after death, but cannot own an act like qisas because it requires capacity to act. Thus, qisas is a right established directly for the heirs after the victim's death, not transferred from him, making it a khilafa. This is a fundamental Hanafi principle in jinayat.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide or injury, a right of the victim's heirs.
خلافة (khilafa): Substitution: the right passes to heirs as representatives of the victim, not as inheritors.
وراثة (waratha): Inheritance: transfer of property rights after death.
خصم (khasm): Litigant or party in a legal proceeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why cannot a present heir represent an absent heir in a qisas case?
A) Because the absent heir is not eligible to own qisas
B) Because qisas is a khilafa, not inheritance, so each heir must establish their own right
C) Because the present heir must first seek permission from the judge
D) Because the deceased has already forgiven the killer

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa’s proof that qisas is a khilafa (substitution) establishes that each heir must individually claim the right to qisas, preventing representation of absent heirs.

Qisas — Retaliation
