Killer's Proof of Forgiveness: Present Heir as Representative
Ruling on killer presenting evidence of absent heir's forgiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that when a killer proves an absent heir's forgiveness, the present heir becomes a representative, and explain the necessity-based reasoning (talil).

Core Idea
When a killer proves an absent heir's forgiveness, the present heir must represent the absent out of necessity — otherwise the claim of transformation to diya could never be heard.

This passage addresses a procedural dilemma in qisas: a killer claims that an absent heir has forgiven him, but that heir is not present to confirm. How can the court proceed? The Hanafi ruling is that the present heir is appointed as a representative for the absent one, purely out of necessity. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the conditions, and the parallel case of a jointly owned slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the killer presenting bayyinah that an absent heir has forgiven him. The ruling is that the present heir becomes a litigant (representative) for the absent, qisas drops, and diya becomes wajib.
The representation is limited to this specific claim; it does not give general authority.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) based on necessity (darurah). The text explicitly states 'la yumkinuhu ithbatu illa bi ithbat al-afw min al-ghaib' — the killer cannot prove his claim without the absent heir's forgiveness being established.
No direct Qur'an or hadith is cited; the ruling is derived from rational necessity (istihsan bi al-darurah).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The killer's claim is that the right of qisas has transformed into a property right (diya) due to forgiveness. Since the transformation depends on the absent's forgiveness, the only way to adjudicate is to let the present heir stand in for the absent. Otherwise, the killer could never prove his claim, leading to injustice.
The text emphasizes 'la yumkinuhu ithbatu' — impossibility of proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (intra-Hanafi difference)
The text mentions that on the slave case, Imam Abu Hanifa follows the same principle, while Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) may differ. The general rule about the present heir representing the absent is accepted by all.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; both views have valid reasoning.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Imam Abu Hanifa's view that the present heir becomes a representative upon proof of forgiveness. The slave case also follows this general rule according to the main text.
The tarjih authority is the source itself (Ashraf al-Hidayah), which adopts Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text

اگر قاتل نے ہینہ قائم کر دی کہ غائب نے مجھے معاف کر دیا ہے تو حاضر خصم ہوگا اور قصاص ساقط ہو جائے گا
فان كان اقام القاتل البيئة ان الغائب قد عفا فالشاهد خصم ويسقط القصاص لانه ادعى على الحاضر سقو حقه في القصاص الى مال ولا يمكنه اثباته الا باثبات العفو من الغائب فينتصب الحاضر خصماً عن الغائب وکذلک عبد بين رجلین قتل عمدا واحد الرجلين غائب فهو على هذا لما بينا
ترجمہ پس اگر قاتل نے بینہ قائم کر دیا کہ غائب نے معاف کر دیا ہے تو حاضر ( خالد ) خصم ہو گا اور قصاص ساقط ہو جائے گا اس ۔ کہ قاتل نے حاضر کے حق کے سقوط کا دعویٰ کیا ہے قصاص میں مال کی جانب اور قاتل کو اس دعویٰ کا اثبات ممکن نہیں مگر غائب کی جانب کو ثابت کرنے کے ساتھ تو حاضر غائب کی جانب سے خصم بنے گا اور ایسے ہی غلام جو دو شخصوں کے درمیان ہو جس کو عمد اقتل کر دیا گیا۔
تشریح اور اگر وہی صورت ہو اور زید ( قاتل ) نے دعوی کر کے دلیل و بعینہ سے یہ ثابت کر دیا ہے کہ ساجد نے مجھے معاف کر دیا ہے تو خالد کو ساجد کی طرف سے خصم شمار کیا جائے گا اور جو فیصلہ خالد کے اوپر ہو گا وہ ساجد کے اوپر بھی شمار کیا جائے گا اور قصاص ساقط ہو کر دیت آجائے گی ۔ لہذا اگر ساجد نے حاضر ہونے کے بعد معافی کا انکار کیا تو اب بدستور دیت واجب رہے گی جو خالد اور ساجد کے درمیان آدھی آدھی ہوگی۔
اور اگر خالد اور ساجد کا مشترک غلام ہو جس کو کسی نے قتل کر دیا اور خالد نے قتل پر پبینہ قائم کیا تو امام صاحب اپنے اصول پر اور صاحبین اپنے اصول پر ہیں۔ اور اگر قاتل نے بینہ سے یہ ثابت کر دیا کہ ساجد نے مجھے معاف کر دیا تو اس کا حکم بھی وہی ہے جو مذکور ہوا۔
سوال یہاں خالد کو ساجد کی جانب سے خصم کیسے مان لیا گیا ہے؟
جواب اس لئے کہ زید یہ دعوی کر رہا ہے کہ خالد کا حق قصاص سے منتقل ہو کر مال بن گیا ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہو سکتا ہے جب کہ زیدیہ ثابت کر دے کہ ساجد نے مجھے معاف کیا ہے تو بر بناء مجبوری خالد کو ساجد کی طرف سے خصم مانا گیا اور خالد کی موجودگی میں زید کا بینہ قبول کرنا پڑا۔
If the killer establishes proof that the absent has forgiven, then the present person becomes a litigant and qisas drops. For if the killer establishes evidence that the absent has forgiven, then the witness (present heir) is a litigant and qisas drops, because he claims against the present the dropping of his right to qisas towards property, and he cannot prove it except by proving the forgiveness from the absent, so the present is appointed as a representative of the absent. Similarly, a slave between two men, intentionally killed, one of the two men is absent – it is upon this, due to what we have explained. Translation: So if the killer establishes evidence that the absent has forgiven, then the present (Khalid) becomes a litigant and qisas drops, because the killer claims the dropping of the present's right from qisas to property, and the killer cannot prove this claim except by proving the forgiveness from the absent, so the present becomes a representative of the absent. And similarly, a slave who is between two people and is intentionally killed, and one of the two is absent – they are upon this difference due to the reason we have stated. Commentary: And if the same situation, and Zayd (killer) claims and establishes with evidence that Sajid has forgiven me, then Khalid will be considered a representative for Sajid, and the judgment given upon Khalid will also be binding upon Sajid, and qisas drops and diya becomes due. So if Sajid after appearing denies the forgiveness, then diya remains wajib, half and half between Khalid and Sajid. And if Khalid and Sajid have a joint slave who is killed, and Khalid establishes proof of the killing, then Imam Sahib follows his principle and the two companions follow theirs. And if the killer establishes with evidence that Sajid has forgiven him, then the ruling is the same as mentioned. Question: Why is Khalid considered a representative for Sajid here? Answer: Because Zayd is claiming that Khalid's right has transformed from qisas to property, and this can only happen if Zayd proves that Sajid has forgiven him. So due to necessity, Khalid is considered a representative for Sajid, and in the presence of Khalid, Zayd's evidence must be accepted.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the killer brings evidence (bayyinah) that an absent heir has forgiven the qisas. Under normal circumstances, a present heir cannot represent an absent heir because qisas is a khilafa. However, when the killer claims that the absent heir's forgiveness transforms the right from qisas to diya (blood money), the present heir becomes a representative for the absent heir out of necessity, otherwise the killer's claim could never be proven. Once the evidence is accepted, the ruling applies to both heirs: qisas is dropped and diya becomes wajib. The same rule applies to a jointly owned slave. The question-answer clarifies the legal reasoning: since the killer’s claim involves a transformation of right, the present heir must stand in for the absent one to allow the case to proceed.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Legal proof, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females.
عفو (afw): Forgiveness of the right to qisas, which transforms it to diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a killer proves that an absent heir has forgiven him, the present heir is appointed as representative out of necessity to avoid procedural impasse; qisas drops and diya becomes due.

Two Heirs Testifying That the Third Has Forgiven: Self-Interest Invalidates Testimony
Ruling on two heirs testifying that the third has forgiven

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony by heirs who benefit financially from their own testimony, and explain the reasoning (sabab) for its invalidity.

Core Idea
Testimony that brings financial benefit to the witness is void in qisas cases.

This passage addresses a conflict-of-interest scenario: two of three heirs of a murder victim testify that the third heir has forgiven the killer. If accepted, this testimony would convert the right of qisas (retaliation) into diya (blood money), benefiting the testifying heirs by removing the possibility of qisas and ensuring they receive property. Imam Muhammad rules that such testimony is invalid because the witnesses stand to gain, and instead the forgiveness is imputed to them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Three heirs of a murder victim; two testify that the third has forgiven the killer. Imam Muhammad's ruling: the testimony is void, and it is considered forgiveness from the two testifiers themselves.
The ruling is clear: the act of testifying is legally ineffective.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the principle that the witnesses are drawing benefit to themselves (yajurran anfusahum) because qisas converts to property, i.e., they stand to gain financially.
The Arabic text explicitly states: 'li'annahum maghnam wa huwa inqilab al-qawd malan yajurran bi shahadatihim anfusahum'.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The testimony is invalid because the witnesses have a personal financial interest in the outcome. This creates a conflict of interest, disqualifying them as witnesses under Hanafi law.
This is a form of reasoning based on the purpose of testimony: it must be unbiased.
4
Consider the practical implications
If the third heir confirms the testimony, the two testifying heirs receive diya; if he denies, they get nothing and he takes his share of diya. The text gives two of four possible scenarios.
The commentary expands to show how the ruling plays out in different fact patterns.
5
Apply the principle broadly
The ruling establishes a general principle: any witness who directly benefits from his own testimony is disqualified in qisas and presumably other cases where property rights are at stake.
This aligns with broader Hanafi rules on witness competence and impartiality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقتول کے تین اولیاء میں سے دو نے گواہی دی کہ تیسرے نے معاف کر دیا ہے تو گواہی ان کی باطل ہے اور معافی ان دو کی طرف سے ہوگی
قال فان كانت الاولياء ثلثة فشهد اثنان منهم على الاخر انه قد عفا فشهادتهما باطلة وهو عفو منهما لانهما مغنما وهو انقلاب القود مالا يجران بشهادتهم انفسهمـ
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا کہ اگر اولیاء تین ہوں پس ان میں سے دو نے دوسرے کے اوپر شہادت دی کہ اس نے معاف کر دیا تو ان دونوں کی شہادت باطل ہے اور یہ معافی ان دونوں کی طرف سے ہو گی اس لئے یہ دونوں اپنی شہادت سے اپنی طرف غنیمت کھینچ رہے ہیں اور وہ قصاص کا مال سے پلٹنا ہے۔
تشریح زید نے بکر کو عمد اقتل کیا تھا لیکن یہاں اس کے تین لڑکے ہیں ، خالد ، ساجد، زاہد دونوں نے گواہی دی کہ زاہد نے اپنا حق معاف کر دیا تو اس کو امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ خالد اور ساجد کی گواہی باطل ہوگی اور معافی خالد اور ساجد ہی کی طرف سے شمار کی جائے گی کیونکہ ان دونوں کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ ہم کو اس طرح کرنے سے بجائے قصاص کے مال مل جائے گا۔
تنبیہ یہ مسئلہ تفصیل طلب ہے جس کی چار صورتیں ہیں: (1) زید ( قاتل) اور زاہد (بھائی) دونوں ان کی تصدیق کر دیں کہ ہاں بات یوں ہی ہے تو چونکہ زاہد نے ان کی تصدیق کر دی تو اس صورت میں زاہد کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ البتہ خالد اور ساجد کو دیت کے دولت ملیں گے۔
زید اور زاہد دونوں نے ان کی تکذیب کر دی تو اب ان دونوں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ اور صرف زاہد کو دیت کا ثلث ۱/۳ ملے گا ان دونوں
Two of the three heirs of the slain testify that the third has forgiven; their testimony is void, and it is a forgiveness from those two. He (Muhammad) said: If the heirs are three, and two of them testify against the other that he has forgiven, then their testimony is void, and it is a forgiveness from those two, because they are drawing benefit to themselves, and it is the conversion of qisas to property, which they bring upon themselves by their own testimony. Translation: Muhammad said: If the heirs are three, and two testify against the third that he has forgiven, then their testimony is void, and it is a forgiveness from those two, because they are drawing benefit (ghaneemat) to themselves by their testimony, which is the conversion of retaliation into property. Commentary: Zayd intentionally killed Bakr. He has three sons: Khalid, Sajid, and Zahid. The two (Khalid and Sajid) testify that Zahid has forgiven his right. Imam Muhammad says: Khalid and Sajid's testimony is void, and the forgiveness is considered from Khalid and Sajid themselves, because their aim is to obtain property instead of qisas. Note: This issue requires detail; it has four scenarios: (1) Zayd (killer) and Zahid (brother) both confirm their statement, then since Zahid confirmed, Zahid gets nothing, but Khalid and Sajid get the diya money. (2) Zayd and Zahid both deny their statement, then they (Khalid and Sajid) get nothing, and only Zahid gets one third of the diya.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where three heirs have a right to qisas. Two of them testify that the third has forgiven the killer. Imam Muhammad rules that their testimony is invalid, and instead they themselves are deemed to have forgiven their own shares. This is because they stand to benefit financially if qisas converts to diya, creating a conflict of interest. The commentator then explains four possible sub-scenarios: (1) If the killer and the third heir confirm their testimony, then the third heir's share of diya is forfeited, and only the two testifying heirs receive diya. (2) If both deny, then the two testifying heirs get nothing, and the third heir takes his full third of diya. (The passage cuts off, indicating further scenarios). This illustrates the Hanafi rule that a witness cannot benefit financially from his own testimony in qisas cases.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony in court; here subject to rules of interest.
غنیمت (ghaneemat): Benefit or gain; the two heirs are drawing benefit to themselves through their testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because they are minors
B) Because they benefit financially from the conversion of qisas to diya
C) Because the third heir is not present in court
D) Because the killer has already confessed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a witness cannot testify if he stands to gain financially from the outcome of the case.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of Heirs Who Benefit from Their Own Testimony is Invalid
Ruling on testimony of two heirs about third's forgiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on two heirs testifying that the third has forgiven the killer, and explain why their testimony is invalid.

Core Idea
Testimony that brings benefit to the witness is rejected; it is treated as forgiveness from the witnesses.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Imam Muhammad in qisas law. When two of three heirs testify that the third has forgiven the killer, they stand to gain blood-money if qisas is converted to diya. The Hanafi school holds their testimony invalid due to self-interest (ghunm) and considers it an act of forgiveness from them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the testimony
The victim has three heirs. Two heirs (witnesses) testify in court that the third heir has forgiven the killer's qisas. What is the effect of their testimony?
Focus on the matn: 'fashahadatuhumā bāṭilah' – their testimony is invalid.
2
Recognize the benefit (ghunm)
The witnesses stand to gain (mughnim) from their testimony: if the forgiveness is established, qisas is converted to blood-money, and they gain a share. This benefit taints the testimony.
The Arabic term 'mughnim' is key.
3
Understand the consequence
Because the testimony is invalid, it is not accepted. Instead, it is treated as forgiveness (ʿafw) emanating from the two witnesses themselves. This drops the qisas right of those two heirs.
The ruling: 'wa huwa ʿafwun minhumā' – and it is forgiveness from them.
4
Note the broader principle
This case illustrates the Hanafi rule that witnesses cannot benefit from their own testimony. The principle is applied specifically when testimony would convert qisas into property gain.
This is a specific application of the general rule against self-interested testimony.

قال فان كانت الاولياء ثلثة فشهد اثنان منهم على الاخر انه قد عفا فشهادتهما باطلة وهو عفو منهما لانهما مغنما وهو انقلاب القود مالا يجران بشهادتهم انفسهم ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا کہ اگر اولیاء تین ہوں پس ان میں سے دو نے دوسرے کے اوپر شہادت دی کہ اس نے معاف کر دیا تو ان دونوں کی شہادت باطل ہے اور یہ معافی ان دونوں کی طرف سے ہو گی اس لئے یہ دونوں اپنی شہادت سے اپنی طرف غنیمت کھینچ رہے ہیں اور وہ قصاص کا مال سے پلٹنا ہے۔ تشریح زید نے بکر کو عمد قتل کیا تھا لیکن یہاں اس کے تین لڑکے ہیں ، خالد ، ساجد، زاہد دونوں نے گواہی دی کہ زاہد نے اپنا حق معاف کر دیا تو اس کو امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ خالد اور ساجد کی گواہی باطل ہوگی اور معافی خالد اور ساجد ہی کی طرف سے شمار کی جائے گی کیونکہ ان دونوں کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ ہم کو اس طرح کرنے سے بجائے قصاص کے مال مل جائے گا۔ تنبیہ یہ مسئلہ تفصیل طلب ہے جس کی چار صورتیں ہیں: (1) زید ( قاتل) اور زاہد (بھائی) دونوں ان کی تصدیق کر دیں کہ ہاں بات یوں ہی ہے تو چونکہ زاہد نے ان کی تصدیق کر دی تو اس صورت میں زاہد کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ البتہ خالد اور ساجد کو دیت کے دوتہائی ملے گا۔ (2) زید اور زاہد دونوں نے ان کی تکذیب کر دی تو اب ان دونوں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ اور صرف زاہد کو دیت کا ثلث ۱/۳ ملے گا۔ (3) صرف زید ( قاتل) نے ان دونوں کی تصدیق کی تو اس صورت میں ان تینوں کو پوری دیت ملے گی اور ہر ایک کو دیت کا تہائی ملے گا۔ (4) زاہد نے ان دونوں کی تصدیق کی اور قاتل نے تکذیب کی تو ان دونوں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا البتہ صرف زاہد کو دیت کا تہائی ملے گا۔ پھر اس ثلث کو وہ دونوں زاہد سے لے لیں گے کیونکہ زاہد نے ان کی تصدیق کی تھی جس سے اس نے اقرار کر لیا تھا کہ حق انہی کا ہے۔ لہذا مصنف فرماتے ہیں۔ قاتل نے دونوں کی تصدیق کر دی تو دیت ان دونوں کے درمیان اثلاثا تقسیم ہوگی فان صدقهما القاتل فالدية بينهما اثلاثا معناه اذا صدقهما وحده لانه لما صدقهما فقد اقر بثلثى الدية لهما فصح اقراره الا انه يدعى سقوط حق المشهود عليه وهو ينكر فلا يصدق ويغرم نصيبه ترجمہ پس اگر قاتل نے دونوں کی تصدیق کر دی تو دیت ان دونوں کے درمیان تین تہائی ہو کر ہوگی۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ ان دونوں کی تصدیق صرف قاتل نے کی ہو اس لئے کہ جب قاتل نے ان دونوں کی تصدیق کر دی تو ان دونوں کے لئے دو تہائی دیت کا اقرار کر لیا تو اس کا اقرار صحیح ہے مگر قاتل مشہود علیہ ( زاہد ) کا حق ساقط ہونے کا دعوی کرتا ہے حالانکہ وہ ( زاہد ) انکار کرتا ہے تو قاتل کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی اور قاتل اس کے (زاہد کے ) حصہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ تشریح یہ تیسری صورت کا حکم ہے جس میں ہر ایک کو دیت ملتی ہے کیونکہ جب زید (قاتل) نے ان دونوں کی تصدیق کی تو گویا ان کے لئے دو ثلث دیت کا اقرار کرلیا تو زید کا یہ اقرار تو درست ہے۔ لیکن زید ساتھ ہی ساتھ یہ بھی دعوی کر رہا ہے ( اپنی تصدیق کی وجہ سے ) کہ زاہد کا حق ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ وہ معاف کر چکا ہے۔ حالانکہ زاہد معافی سے انکار کرتا ہے تو اس میں زید کا قول معتبر نہ ہوگا ۔ ( اور زاہد کے حصہ کی دیت بھی اس پر واجب ہوگی۔ اگر قاتل نے دونوں کی تکذیب کر دی تو تیسرے کے لئے ایک تہائی دیت ہوگی اور ان دونوں کے لئے کچھ نہ ہوگا وان كذبهما فلاشئى لهما وللاخر ثلث الدية معناه اذا كذبهما القاتل ايضاً وهذا لانهما اقرا على انفسهم بسقوط القصاص فقبل و ادعيا انقلاب نصيبهما مالا فلايقبل الا بحجة وينقلب نصيب المشهود عليه مالا لان دعواهما العفو عليه وهو منكر بمنزلة ابتداء العفو منهما فى حق المشهود عليه لان سقوط القود مضاف اليهما ترجمہ اور اگر زاهد نے ان دونوں کی تکذیب کر دی ہو تو ان دونوں کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرے زاہد کے لئے تہائی دیت ہے اس کے معنی یہ ہیں جب کہ قاتل نے بھی ان دونوں کی تکذیب کی ہو اور یہ اس لئے کہ ان دونوں نے اپنے نفسوں پر قصاص کے سقوط کا اقرار کیا ہے تو یہ اقرار مقبول ہو گا اور ان دونوں نے اپنے حصہ کے مال سے پلٹنے کا دعوی کیا ہے تو یہ اقرار قبول نہ ہو گا مگر حجت کی وجہ سے ہے اور مشہود علیہ کا حصہ مال سے بدل جائے گا اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کا مشہود علیہ پر عفو کا دعوی کرنا حالانکہ وہ منکر ہے مشہود علیہ کے حق میں ان دونوں کی جانب سے ابتدا بعفو کے درجہ میں ہے اس لئے قصاص کا سقوط انہیں دونوں کی طرف مضاف ہے۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: If the heirs are three, and two of them testify against the third that he has forgiven, then their testimony is invalid, and it is forgiveness from them, because they are drawing gain (mughnim) to themselves by their testimony, and that is the conversion of qisas into property. Translation: Muhammad said: If there are three heirs, and two of them testify against the third that he has forgiven, then their testimony is invalid, and forgiveness is from them, because these two are drawing gain to themselves by their testimony, and that is the conversion of qisas into property. Commentary: Zaid had intentionally killed Bakr, but here he has three sons: Khalid, Sajid, Zahid. The two testified that Zahid had forgiven his right. So Imam Muhammad said: The testimony of Khalid and Sajid is invalid, and the forgiveness will be counted from Khalid and Sajid themselves, because their intention is that by doing so they will get property instead of qisas. Note: This issue has details with four scenarios: (1) If Zaid (the killer) and Zahid (the brother) both confirm them, then because Zahid confirmed, he gets nothing, but Khalid and Sajid get two-thirds of the blood-money. (2) If Zaid and Zahid both deny them, then those two get nothing, and only Zahid gets one-third of the blood-money. (3) If only Zaid (the killer) confirms them, then all three get the full blood-money, each getting one-third. (4) If Zahid confirms them and the killer denies, then those two get nothing, only Zahid gets one-third, but then those two take that third from Zahid because Zahid had confirmed them, thereby acknowledging that the right is theirs. Hence the author says: If the killer confirms the two, the blood-money is divided among them in thirds. Meaning when he alone confirms them, because when he confirms them, he has acknowledged two-thirds of the blood-money for them, so his acknowledgment is valid, except that he claims the right of the testified-against (Zahid) has fallen, while he (Zahid) denies, so he is not believed and he (the killer) guarantees his share. Commentary: This is the ruling of the third scenario where each gets blood-money, because when Zaid confirmed them, he acknowledged two-thirds of the blood-money for them, so Zaid's acknowledgment is correct, but Zaid also claims that Zahid's right has fallen because he has forgiven, while Zahid denies forgiveness, so Zaid's statement is not believed, and he is liable for Zahid's share. If the killer denies both, then the third gets one-third of the blood-money and those two get nothing. And if he denies both, those two get nothing and the other gets one-third of the blood-money. Meaning when the killer also denies them. This is because those two have acknowledged upon themselves the fall of qisas, so it is accepted, and they claim conversion of their share into property, so it is not accepted except with proof, and the share of the testified-against is converted into property because their claim of forgiveness upon him while he denies is like initiating forgiveness from them in the right of the testified-against, because the fall of qisas is attributed to them.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on a specific scenario in qisas (retaliation) law. The matn, attributed to Imam Muhammad, states that if a victim has three heirs and two of them testify that the third has forgiven the killer, their testimony is invalid. The reason is that they stand to benefit from this testimony: if the forgiveness is established, qisas is converted into blood-money (diya), and they gain property instead of retaliation. Therefore, their testimony is rejected due to self-interest, and the testimony itself is treated as forgiveness emanating from them (the two witnesses) towards the killer. The commentary then elaborates four possible sub-scenarios based on whether the killer and the third heir confirm or deny the testimony. The key principle is that witnesses cannot benefit from their own testimony in criminal cases. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
اولیاء (awliyā'): In this context, the heirs of the victim who have the right to demand qisas or accept blood-money.
عفو (ʿafw): Forgiveness or pardon of the right to qisas, which converts the claim to blood-money if done by all heirs.
مغنم (mughnim): Something that brings gain or benefit; here, the witnesses' testimony brings them material benefit (blood-money).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the victim has three heirs, and two testify that the third has forgiven the killer, what is the ruling on their testimony?
A) The testimony is valid and the killer is free.
B) The testimony is valid and qisas is imposed.
C) The testimony is invalid and it counts as forgiveness from the two witnesses.
D) The testimony is invalid and the two witnesses are punished for false testimony.

Key Takeaway
When heirs testify about another heir's forgiveness for the killer, their testimony is invalid and treated as their own forgiveness because they benefit from the conversion of qisas to diya.

Qisas — Retaliation
advanced
12 min
Detailed Scenarios When Two Heirs Testify
Detailed scenarios of testimony and blood-money distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on disputed testimony to the four sub-scenarios based on confirmation or denial by the killer and the third heir, and determine the distribution of blood-money.

Core Idea
The ruling's application depends on whether the killer and the third heir confirm or deny the testimony, affecting shares of blood-money.

The commentary on Imam Muhammad's ruling details four possible responses to the two heirs' testimony. Depending on whether the killer and the third heir confirm or deny, the distribution of blood-money changes. This lesson unpacks each scenario and the underlying legal reasoning, helping you apply the principle in practice.

Guided Path
1
List the four permutations
The two variables: the killer's reaction (confirm or deny) and the third heir's reaction (confirm or deny). This gives four combinations. Write them down.
The commentary uses 'tasdiq' (confirmation) and 'takdhib' (denial).
2
Apply the principle to each scenario
For each combination, determine the outcome for the two witnesses' claim to diya and the third heir's share. The key is that the two witnesses' testimony is invalid, so their claim of forgiveness is not accepted unless independently confirmed.
The outcomes: (1) Both confirm → witnesses get 2/3, third gets nothing. (2) Both deny → witnesses get nothing, third gets 1/3. (3) Killer only confirms → all three get 1/3 each. (4) Third only confirms → witnesses get nothing, third gets 1/3, but then witnesses take that 1/3 from third because his confirmation is an admission.
3
Understand the reasoning behind scenario 3
When the killer alone confirms the witnesses, he is acknowledging that they have a right to 2/3 of the diya. But he also claims that the third heir's right has fallen (due to forgiveness). Since the third heir denies, the killer is not trusted regarding that, and so the killer must guarantee the third's share.
This creates a full diya for all three: each gets 1/3, but the killer is liable for the third's share if the third doesn't get it.
4
Understand the reasoning behind scenario 4
When the third heir alone confirms the witnesses, he is essentially admitting that his own right to qisas has fallen (forgiveness). This is treated as his own forgiveness, so he receives nothing. However, the witnesses, having testified invalidly, also receive nothing. But the third's confirmation is an admission that the witnesses deserve his share, so they can take his 1/3 diya from him.
Here, the witnesses gain the third's share because of his admission, even though their testimony was invalid.

حصہ کی دیت بھی اس پر واجب ہوگی۔ اگر قاتل نے دونوں کی تکذیب کر دی تو تیسرے کے لئے ایک تہائی دیت ہوگی اور ان دونوں کے لئے کچھ نہ ہوگا وان كذبهما فلاشئى لهما وللاخر ثلث الدية معناه اذا كذبهما القاتل عليه لان سقوط القود مضاف اليهما ترجمہ اور اگر زاهد نے ان دونوں کی تکذیب کر دی ہو تو ان دونوں کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسرے زاہد کے لئے تہائی دیت ہے اس کے معنی یہ ہیں جب کہ قاتل نے بھی ان دونوں کی تکذیب کی ہو اور یہ اس لئے کہ ان دونوں نے اپنے نفسوں پر قصاص کے سقوط کا اقرار کیا ہے تو یہ اقرار مقبول ہو گا اور ان دونوں نے اپنے حصہ کے مال سے پلٹنے کا دعوی کیا ہے تو یہ اقرار قبول نہ ہو گا مگر حجت کی وجہ سے ہے اور مشہود علیہ کا حصہ مال سے بدل جائے گا اس لئے کہ ان دونوں کا مشہود علیہ پر عفو کا دعوی کرنا حالانکہ وہ منکر ہے مشہود علیہ کے حق میں ان دونوں کی جانب سے ابتدا بعفو کے درجہ میں ہے اس لئے قصاص کا سقوط انہیں دونوں کی طرف مضاف ہے۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: If the heirs are three, and two of them testify against the third that he has forgiven, then their testimony is invalid, and it is forgiveness from them, because they are drawing gain (mughnim) to themselves by their testimony, and that is the conversion of qisas into property. Translation: Muhammad said: If there are three heirs, and two of them testify against the third that he has forgiven, then their testimony is invalid, and forgiveness is from them, because these two are drawing gain to themselves by their testimony, and that is the conversion of qisas into property. Commentary: Zaid had intentionally killed Bakr, but here he has three sons: Khalid, Sajid, Zahid. The two testified that Zahid had forgiven his right. So Imam Muhammad said: The testimony of Khalid and Sajid is invalid, and the forgiveness will be counted from Khalid and Sajid themselves, because their intention is that by doing so they will get property instead of qisas. Note: This issue has details with four scenarios: (1) If Zaid (the killer) and Zahid (the brother) both confirm them, then because Zahid confirmed, he gets nothing, but Khalid and Sajid get two-thirds of the blood-money. (2) If Zaid and Zahid both deny them, then those two get nothing, and only Zahid gets one-third of the blood-money. (3) If only Zaid (the killer) confirms them, then all three get the full blood-money, each getting one-third. (4) If Zahid confirms them and the killer denies, then those two get nothing, only Zahid gets one-third, but then those two take that third from Zahid because Zahid had confirmed them, thereby acknowledging that the right is theirs. Hence the author says: If the killer confirms the two, the blood-money is divided among them in thirds. Meaning when he alone confirms them, because when he confirms them, he has acknowledged two-thirds of the blood-money for them, so his acknowledgment is valid, except that he claims the right of the testified-against (Zahid) has fallen, while he (Zahid) denies, so he is not believed and he (the killer) guarantees his share. Commentary: This is the ruling of the third scenario where each gets blood-money, because when Zaid confirmed them, he acknowledged two-thirds of the blood-money for them, so Zaid's acknowledgment is correct, but Zaid also claims that Zahid's right has fallen because he has forgiven, while Zahid denies forgiveness, so Zaid's statement is not believed, and he is liable for Zahid's share. If the killer denies both, then the third gets one-third of the blood-money and those two get nothing. And if he denies both, those two get nothing and the other gets one-third of the blood-money. Meaning when the killer also denies them. This is because those two have acknowledged upon themselves the fall of qisas, so it is accepted, and they claim conversion of their share into property, so it is not accepted except with proof, and the share of the testified-against is converted into property because their claim of forgiveness upon him while he denies is like initiating forgiveness from them in the right of the testified-against, because the fall of qisas is attributed to them.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on a specific scenario in qisas (retaliation) law. The matn, attributed to Imam Muhammad, states that if a victim has three heirs and two of them testify that the third has forgiven the killer, their testimony is invalid. The reason is that they stand to benefit from this testimony: if the forgiveness is established, qisas is converted into blood-money (diya), and they gain property instead of retaliation. Therefore, their testimony is rejected due to self-interest, and the testimony itself is treated as forgiveness emanating from them (the two witnesses) towards the killer. The commentary then elaborates four possible sub-scenarios based on whether the killer and the third heir confirm or deny the testimony. The key principle is that witnesses cannot benefit from their own testimony in criminal cases. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
اولیاء (awliyā'): In this context, the heirs of the victim who have the right to demand qisas or accept blood-money.
عفو (ʿafw): Forgiveness or pardon of the right to qisas, which converts the claim to blood-money if done by all heirs.
مغنم (mughnim): Something that brings gain or benefit; here, the witnesses' testimony brings them material benefit (blood-money).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the killer and the third heir both deny the two witnesses' testimony, what is the distribution of blood-money?
A) The witnesses get 2/3, the third gets 1/3.
B) The witnesses get nothing, the third gets 1/3.
C) All three get 1/3 each.
D) The witnesses get nothing, the killer is free.

Key Takeaway
The distribution of blood-money in this case depends entirely on whether the killer and third heir confirm or deny the invalid testimony, reflecting nuanced rules of admission and liability.

Distinguishing Mujmal and Mutlaq: Application in Qatl Rulings
Defines mujmal and mutlaq in context of qatl rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mujmal and mutlaq, and apply the distinction to determine whether a legal term requires clarification before action.

Core Idea
Mujmal is ambiguous and needs clarification; mutlaq is clear in essence though multiple individuals are possible.

In studying the ruling on intentional killing (qatl 'amad), the author pauses to clarify a crucial usul distinction. The cautionary note (tanbih) defines two types of textual terms: mujmal (ambiguous) and mutlaq (absolute). Understanding this difference is essential for interpreting legal texts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Contextualize the Passage
Recognize that the author first states that the killing in question is construed as 'amad (intentional) and then inserts a tanbih (cautionary note). This note distinguishes between mujmal and mutlaq, highlighting that the distinction affects how we understand the earlier ruling.
The tanbih is a parenthetical clarification, not directly part of the homicide discussion.
2
Define Mujmal
Identify the characteristics: mujmal is a term that has ambiguity among several possible meanings, and the intended essence (dhat) is not known. It cannot be acted upon until evidence specifies one meaning.
Hanafi usul: mujmal requires bayan (clarification).
3
Define Mutlaq
Identify the characteristics: mutlaq is a term with a known meaning, but its scope includes multiple individuals of different types. It can be acted upon immediately because the essence is known.
Hanafi: mutlaq is applied as is unless there is evidence for taqyid (restriction).
4
Analyze the Example
The cow of the Children of Israel is given as an example of mutlaq: any cow, regardless of color or age, would suffice for the sacrifice. The hadith indicates that by asking for specifics, they made it difficult for themselves.
This illustrates that acting on a mutlaq command is valid and permissible.
5
Apply to Qatl Context
Link the distinction back to the homicide ruling: the term 'qatl' in the earlier statement is being interpreted as 'amad (intentional). This interpretation is based on the principle that when a term is mutlaq, it is taken in its absolute sense unless specified otherwise.
The tanbih ensures the reader understands the methodological basis for the ruling.

Source Text

لئے کہ اس قتل کو قتل عمد پر محمول کیا جائے گا کیونکہ قتل میں اول عمد ہے اور عمد کا ضمان برادری پر نہیں ہوتا ۔ تنبیہ مجمل ومطلق میں فرق ہے مجمل وہ جس میں چند معانی میں اشتباہ ہو اور ذات معلوم نہ ہو۔ پھر اگر کسی دلیل سے کوئی معنی متعین ہو جائے تو اس پر عمل ہوگا۔ اور مطلق وہ ہے کہ اس کے معنی معلوم ہوتے ہیں لیکن اس کے ثبوت میں کئی فرد مختلف الاصناف مندرج ہوتے ہیں تو کسی بھی فرد کو لے لیا جائے بہر حال مطلق پر عمل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ ذات معلوم ہے جیسے بنی اسرائیل کا بقرہ مطلق ہے خواہ کوئی رنگ ہو یا کوئی عمر ہو لہذا اس پر عمل ممکن ہے۔ اسی واسطے حدیث میں آیا ہے کہ اس حکم کے وقت بنی اسرائیل جس کسی گائے کو قربان کرتے تو جائز ہو جاتا لیکن ان لوگوں نے سختی کی تو اللہ نے ان پر سخت کر دیا۔
Because this killing will be construed as intentional killing, because in killing, first is intentional, and the responsibility for intentional is not on the brotherhood. A note: there is a difference between mujmal and mutlaq. Mujmal is that which has ambiguity among several meanings and the essence is not known. Then if some evidence specifies a meaning, it will be acted upon. And mutlaq is that whose meaning is known, but in its proof several individuals of different types are included, so any individual may be taken; in any case, the mutlaq will be acted upon because the essence is known, like the cow of the Children of Israel is mutlaq, whether any color or any age, so action upon it is possible. For that reason, it has come in the hadith that at the time of that command, the Children of Israel would sacrifice any cow and it would be valid, but those people made it difficult, so Allah made it difficult for them.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explanation distinguishing between two important legal terms: mujmal (ambiguous) and mutlaq (absolute). The author first notes that the previous discussion about intentional killing is being construed as 'amad (intentional), and then gives a cautionary note (tanbih) defining mujmal and mutlaq. Mujmal is a term with multiple possible meanings and the intended referent is not known; it cannot be acted upon until clarified by evidence. Mutlaq is a term with a known meaning that covers multiple individuals; it can be acted upon immediately, as illustrated by the story of the cow in the Qur'an where the Israelites were commanded to sacrifice a cow (mutlaq) and any cow would suffice. The hadith mentioned shows that they made the matter difficult by asking for specifics, leading to a stricter command. This distinction is foundational in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and is applied here in the context of homicide rulings.

Key Terms
مجمل (mujmal): A term that is ambiguous among several meanings and the intended essence (dhat) is not known without clarification.
مطلق (muṭlaq): A term with a known meaning that includes multiple individuals of different types, and can be acted upon as is.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between mujmal and mutlaq?
A) Mujmal has a known essence; mutlaq does not.
B) Mujmal is ambiguous in meaning and essence; mutlaq has a known essence but includes multiple individuals.
C) Both are the same.
D) Mujmal comes from the Qur'an; mutlaq comes from the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Mujmal requires clarification before action; mutlaq can be acted upon immediately because its essence is known.

Confession vs Testimony in Qisas: Effect of Guardian's Denial
States rule and explains difference between iqrar and shahada in qatl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahada) regarding the effect of the guardian's denial (takdhib) in qisas cases.

Core Idea
Denial makes a witness fasiq and voids his testimony, but does not affect the validity of a confession.

This passage presents a nuanced rule in qisas (retribution) cases: when two people confess to the same murder and the guardian says both are liars, both confessions stand and qisas can be exacted. But if two sets of witnesses testify against two different accused and the guardian says both groups are lying, all testimony becomes invalid. The commentary explains that the difference lies in how immorality (fisq) affects confession versus testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage carefully to identify the two cases: (1) two individuals each confess to the killing; (2) two groups of witnesses testify against two different accused persons.
In both, the guardian alleges that both are lying (takdhib).
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
Note the outcome: in the first case, the guardian may exact qisas from both confessors. In the second case, all testimony is void and no qisas is possible.
3
Analyze the effect of denial
Understand that denial (takdhib) by the guardian is considered tafsiq (declaring the confessor/witness to be immoral). However, the legal effect differs.
4
Apply the principle of fisq to each
A confessor becoming fasiq does not invalidate his confession – his admission remains binding. A witness becoming fasiq invalidates his testimony because witness uprightness ('adalah) is a condition for accepting shahada.
Hanafi law accepts iqrar even from a fasiq, but rejects shahada from a fasiq.
5
Conclude the wisdom behind the difference
The rationale is that confession is an admission against one's own interest, which is strong evidence; testimony is a statement about another, requiring probity. Thus, the same denial affects them differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو شخصوں میں سے ہر ایک نے قتل کا اقرار کیا کہ میں نے نقل کیا اور ولی نے کہا کہ تم دونوں نے قتل کیا تو ولی کو قصاصا دونوں کو قتل کرنے کا حق ہے دو آدمیوں نے ایک شخص کے خلاف گواہی دی کہ اس نے زید کو قتل کیا ہے مگر زید کے ولی نے کہا کہ تم دونوں نے قتل کیا ہے تو قصاص کا حکم

قال واذا اقر رجلان كل واحد منهما انه قتل فلانا فقال الولى قتلتماه جميعا فله ان يقتلهما وان شهدو اعلى رجل انه قتل فلانا و شهد اخرون على اخر بقتله وقال الولى قتلتما جميعا بطل ذلك كله

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جب کہ دو شخصوں نے ان میں سے ہر ایک نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ انہوں نے فلاں کو قتل کیا ہے پس ولی نے کہا کہ تم دونوں نے اس کو قتل کیا ہے تو ولی کو حق ہے کہ ان دونوں کو قتل کرے اور اگر انہوں نے کسی شخص کے خلاف گواہی دی کہ اس نے فلاں کو قتل کیا ہے اور دوسرے نے اس کے قتل کی دوسرے پر گواہی دی اور ولی نے کہا کہ تم دونوں نے اس کو قتل کیا ہے تو یہ سب باطل ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح زید نے اقرار کیا کہ میں نے بکر کو قتل کیا ہے اور خالد نے یہ اقرار کیا کہ میں نے بکر کو قتل کیا ہے، زید اور خالد سے ولی نے کہا کہ تم دونوں نے قتل کیا ہے لہذا ولی کو حق ہوگا کہ زید اور خالد دونوں سے قصاص لے۔ اور اگر زید اور خالد دونوں نے گواہی دی کہ بکر کو ساجد نے قتل کیا ہے اور عمر اور خالد نے گواہی دی کہ بکر کو زاہد نے قتل کیا ہے اب ولی کہتا ہے کہ ان سب گواہوں نے بکر کو قتل کیا ہے تو اب ولی کسی سے بھی قصاص نہیں لے سکتا۔

اقرار اور شہادت میں فرق کیوں ہے اس کی وجہ آگے آرہی ہے۔

اقرار اور شہادت کے درمیان وجہ فرق

والفرق ان الاقرار والشهادة يتناول كل واحد منهما وجود كل القتل ووجوب القصاص وقد حصل التكذيب فى الأول من المقرله وفى الثانى من المشهود له غيران تكذيب المقرله المقر فى بعض ما اقربه لا يبطل اقراره فى الباقى وتكذيب المشهود له الشاهد فى بعض ما شهد به يبطل شهادته اصلا لان التكذيب تفسيق وفسق لقبول اما فسق الــمــقــر لا يـمـنـع صحة الاقرار .

ترجمہ اور فرق یہ ہے کہ اقرار و شہادت ان میں سے ہر ایک پورے قتل کے وجود کو اور پورے قصاص کے وجوب کو شامل ہے، اور اول میں مقرلہ کی جانب سے تکذیب حاصل ہو گئی۔ اور ثانی میں مشہودلہ کی جانب سے علاوہ اس باتے کہ مقرلہ کا جھٹلانا مقر کو ان بعض باتوں میں جس کا اس نے اقرار کیا ہے باقی میں اس کے اقرار کو باطل نہیں کرے گا۔ اور مشہودلہ کا جھٹلانا شاہد کو ان بعض باتوں میں جس کی اس نے گواہی دی اس کی شہادت کو بالکل باطل کر دے گا اس لئے کہ تکذیب تفسیق ہے اور شاہد کا فسق قبول شہادت کو روکتا ہے، بہر حال مقر کا فسق اقرار کی صحت کو نہیں روکتا۔

تشریح یہ اقرار و شہادت کے درمیان وجہ فرق ہے۔ ان دونوں کا اقرار یہ بتا رہا تھا کہ پورا قتل ایک کی جانب سے ہے ولی نے ان کی تکذیب کر دی تو جھٹلانے کی وجہ سے وہ فاسق ہوئے اور فاسق کا اقرار صحیح ہوا کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کو قصاص میں قتل کیا جا سکتا ہے اور گواہوں کے دونوں فریق میں سے ہر ایک نے یہ گواہی دی کہ قصاص فلاں پر واجب ہے، ولی نے گواہوں کی بھی تکذیب کی اور جب گواہوں کی تکذیب کی تو وہ فاسق ہو گئے اور فاسق کی گواہی غیر معتبر ہوتی ہے۔
If two men each confess that he killed so-and-so, and the guardian says, 'You both killed him,' then he has the right to kill both. And if they testify against a man that he killed so-and-so, and others testify against another that he killed him, and the guardian says, 'You both killed him,' all of that is void.

Translation: Muhammad said: And when two men each confess that they killed so-and-so, then the guardian says you both killed him, then the guardian has the right to kill both. And if they testify against a man that he killed so-and-so, and others testify against another for his killing, and the guardian says you both killed him, then all of that becomes void.

Explanation: Zaid confessed that he killed Bakr, and Khalid confessed that he killed Bakr. The guardian says to Zaid and Khalid: you both killed him. So the guardian has the right to exact qisas from both. And if Zaid and Khalid both testified that Bakr was killed by Sajid, and Umar and Khalid testified that Bakr was killed by Zahid, and the guardian says all these witnesses killed Bakr, then the guardian cannot take qisas from anyone.

Why is there a difference between confession and testimony? The reason is coming.

The reason for the difference between confession and testimony:

The difference is that confession and testimony each encompass the existence of the entire killing and the obligation of qisas. In the first case (confession), the denial (takdhib) comes from the one to whom the confession is made (al-muqarr lahu). In the second case (testimony), the denial comes from the one for whom the testimony is given (al-mashhud lahu). However, the denial by the muqarr lahu of the confessor regarding some of what he confessed does not invalidate his confession in the remainder. But the denial by the mashhud lahu of the witness regarding some of what he testified invalidates his testimony entirely, because denial is tafsiq (declaring immoral), and the witness's immorality prevents acceptance of testimony. However, the confessor's immorality does not prevent the validity of confession.

Translation: The difference is that confession and testimony each encompass the entire existence of the killing and the obligation of qisas. In the first, denial occurs from the muqarr lahu; in the second, from the mashhud lahu. Besides that, the muqarr lahu's denial of the confessor in some of what he confessed does not invalidate his confession in the remainder. But the mashhud lahu's denial of the witness in some of what he testified invalidates his testimony entirely, because denial is tafsiq, and the witness's immorality prevents acceptance of testimony. However, the confessor's immorality does not prevent the validity of confession.

Explanation: This is the reason for the difference between confession and testimony. The confession of both indicated that the entire killing was from one side. The guardian denied them, so due to denial they became fasiq, and the confession of a fasiq is valid. Therefore, both can be killed in qisas. And the two groups of witnesses each testified that qisas is obligatory on so-and-so. The guardian also denied the witnesses, and when the witnesses are denied, they become fasiq, and the testimony of a fasiq is invalid.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling from Imam Muhammad in the matn: if two individuals each confess to killing a person, and the guardian says both killed, the guardian may execute both in qisas. However, if two separate groups of witnesses testify against two different accused persons, and the guardian says both groups killed, then all testimony becomes void and no qisas is possible. The commentary then explains the underlying legal rationale: the key lies in the nature of denial (takdhib). When the guardian denies the confessors, they become fasiq (immoral), but a fasiq's confession remains valid in Hanafi law—immorality does not affect the legal validity of one's own admission. However, when the guardian denies witnesses, they become fasiq, and a fasiq's testimony is not accepted because witness credibility is essential for adjudication. Thus, the difference arises from the distinct legal statuses of confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahada) regarding the effect of the denier's allegation. The practical consequence: in the first scenario, qisas applies; in the second, it is dropped entirely.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrār): A statement by a person admitting a fact against himself, here confession of killing.
شہادت (shahādat): Testimony given by a witness in favor of or against a party.
تکذیب (takdhīb): The act of denying (alleging falsehood) by the guardian against the confessor or witness.
فسق (fisq): Moral depravity or sinfulness that disqualifies a witness but not a confessor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the guardian's denial (takdhib) invalidate testimony but not confession?
A) Because confession is stronger evidence than testimony.
B) Because denial makes the witness fasiq, and a fasiq's testimony is rejected; a confessor's fisq does not invalidate his confession.
C) Because the guardian is not allowed to deny a confession.
D) Because testimony requires two witnesses, while confession requires only one.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the guardian's denial makes witnesses fasiq (voiding their testimony), but confessors remain valid despite becoming fasiq because confession does not require moral uprightness.

Diya When Target Apostatizes After Shooting: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on diya with qiyas reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on diya when the target apostatizes after being shot, and analyze the qiyas reasoning used by the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Apostasy after the act forfeits inviolability, exonerating the shooter in the Sahibayn's view.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on a nuanced temporal question: if a Muslim shoots another Muslim, but the target apostatizes before the arrow strikes, does the shooter owe diya? Abu Hanifa says yes; the Sahibayn say no. The Sahibayn's reasoning employs a qiyas on explicit exoneration (ibrā'), arguing that apostasy, like a pardon, extinguishes the inviolability that grounds liability. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists weigh the moment of liability fixation versus the victim's status at death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is shooting an arrow at a Muslim; the target apostatizes between the shooting and the arrow's impact. Determine what ruling each imam gives for diya.
Abu Hanifa: diya wajib; Sahibayn: no diya.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's qiyas
They analogize apostasy to explicit exoneration (ibrā') after wounding but before death. Identify the asl (original case), the far' (new case), and the illa (common cause).
Asl: victim exonerates shooter; hukm: no diya. Far': victim apostatizes. Illa: forfeiture of taqawwum nafs.
3
Consider Abu Hanifa's counterview
Although the text does not give Abu Hanifa's explicit dalīl, infer it: liability attached at the moment of shooting when the target was still a protected Muslim. The subsequent apostasy does not retroactively remove that liability.
This is a classic difference on the temporal assignment of liability: act initiation vs final status.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the shooter pays diya; under Sahibayn, the shooter pays nothing. This affects the application of qisas and diyat in cases where the victim's religious status changes between act and death.
Important for fatwa: the mufta bihi in later Hanafi works often follows Abu Hanifa, but both positions are recorded.

بَابُ فِي اعْتِبار حالة القتل

ترجمہ یہ باب حالت قتل کو اعتبار کرنے کے بیان میں ہے

تشریح احوال از قبیل صفات ہیں اور ذوات صفات سے مقدم ہوتی ہے اس وجہ سے قتل کے ذکر کے بعد احوال کا ذکر فرمایا گیا ہے۔ مسلمان نے تیر پھینکا جس کی طرف پھینکا وہ تیر لگنے کے بعد مرتد ہو گیا را می پردیت ہے

قال ومن رمى مسلما فارتد المرمى اليه والعياذ بالله ثم وقع به السهم فعلى الرامي الداية عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا شئى عليه لانه بالارتداد اسقط تقوم نفسه فيكون مبرئا للرامى عن موجبه كما اذا ابرأه بعد الجرح قبل الموت

تو اس میں امام ابوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے امام صاحب کے نزدیک زید پر دیت واجب ہوگی۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک کچھ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Chapter on considering the state of killing.

Translation: This chapter is about considering the state of killing.

Explanation: States (ahwal) are of the type of qualities, and they precede essences (dhawat). For this reason, after mentioning killing, the states are mentioned. A Muslim shot an arrow; the one at whom he shot became an apostate (may Allah protect us), then the arrow struck him. So the shooter owes diya according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: nothing is owed to him, because by apostasy he forfeited the inviolability (taqawwum) of his life, thus he exonerates the shooter from its consequence, just as if he had exonerated him after the wound before death.

Translation: Muhammad said: And whoever shot at a Muslim, then the target became an apostate, then the arrow struck him, then the shooter owes diya according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions said: nothing is owed to him, because by apostasy he forfeited the inviolability of his life, so the apostate becomes one who exonerates the shooter from its consequence, like when he exonerated him after the wound before death.

Explanation: Amr is a person who is a Muslim, but he argues with trustworthy Muslims about religious matters. Then during the conversation, he reveals his inner disbelief. But Zaid does not know any of this, and he shoots an arrow at Amr. At the time of shooting, his apostasy had not become apparent, but at the time of impact (when the arrow struck), he had already apostatized. What is the ruling? In this, there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions. According to Imam, diya is obligatory on Zaid. According to the two, nothing is obligatory.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage introduces a new chapter on considering the state (hal) of the victim at the time of killing. The author notes that states (ahwal) are qualities and precede essences in consideration, hence this chapter follows the general discussion on killing. The specific case: a Muslim shoots an arrow at another Muslim, but between the shooting and the impact, the target apostatizes (becomes murtad). The ruling: Abu Hanifa holds that the shooter must pay diya (blood money), because liability was established at the time of the act (ramy) when the target was still a protected Muslim. The two followers (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no diya is due, because the apostate has forfeited the inviolability of his life (taqawwum nafsihi) by apostasy, effectively exonerating the shooter, analogous to a case where the victim explicitly exonerates the shooter after being wounded but before death. The commentary illustrates with an example: Amr argues about religion and reveals inner kufr, but Zaid, unaware, shoots. At the moment of shooting, Amr is still Muslim in external status; at impact, he is murtad. The ikhtilaf hinges on whether the liability attaches at the time of the act or the time of death. Abu Hanifa looks at the act's initiation; Sahibayn consider the victim's status at death. This difference is a classic intra-Hanafi dispute with practical implications for diya liability.

Key Terms
ارتداد (irtidād): Apostasy from Islam; in this context, it forfeits the inviolability of life.
دیت (diya): Blood money or financial compensation due for unlawful killing (not intentional).
تقوم (taqawwum): The inviolability or monetary value assigned to a human life (here: the basis for diya).
صاحبین (Ṣāḥibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the primary students of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because diya is never due for an apostate.
D) Because the arrow missed.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on diya when the target apostatizes after the shooting hinges on whether liability is fixed at the moment of the act (Abu Hanifa) or at the time of death (Sahibayn), using qiyas on explicit exoneration.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qisas in Pre-Mudihah Wounds
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for pre-mudihah wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas in pre-mudihah wounds and state the mufta bihi position with its proof.

Core Idea
For pre-mudihah wounds, equality can be measured, making qisas wajib—unless the wound has no defined limit.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi difference regarding qisas for wounds less severe than mudihah. While one narration from Abu Hanifa holds that exact retaliation is impossible due to the lack of a defined wound boundary, the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) asserts that equality can be achieved through measurement. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes practical possibility over theoretical objection.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position according to Zahir al-Riwayah
Identify what the relied-upon transmitted position says regarding qisas for pre-mudihah wounds and the reasoning provided.
This is the view recorded in the six core books of Imam Muhammad, considered the highest authority in the school.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi narration
Locate the alternative view attributed to Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) and understand its basis.
This is a rarer transmission, not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Examine why the opposing narration argues that qisas is not possible: the lack of a defined endpoint for the wound makes exact retaliation unattainable.
The objection focuses on the practical impossibility of musawat (equality).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response from Zahir al-Riwayah
Understand how the relied-upon position rebuts this objection by describing a method to achieve equality: measuring wound depth with a probe and cutting exactly that amount.
The illa of impossibility is not present because measurement is feasible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical consequence of the dispute: according to one view, the offender undergoes qisas; according to the other, he pays hukumat al-adl. State which view is operative for fatwa.
The mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah position: qisas is wajib.

ٹوٹتی ہے اور ماقبل میں مسئلہ گزرچکا ہے کہ ہڈیوں میں قصاص نہیں ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام امام ابو حنیفہ کی اس روایت کے مطابق موضحہ سے اوپر جو چھ مذکور ہیں نہ ان میں قصاص ہے اور نہ ان تین میں جو موضحہ کے بعد مذکور خوف هلاک غالب فيسبر غورها بمسلة [؟] ثم يتحد حديدة بقدر ذالك فيقطع بها مقدار ما قطع فيتحقق استيفاء القصاص ترجمہ اور یہ ایک روایت ہے ابوحنیفہ سے اور محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا ہے اور یہی ظاہر الروایہ ہے کہ ان زخموں میں جو موضحہ سے پہلے ہیں قصاص واجب ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں مساوات کا اعتبار ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں بڑی تو ڑنا نہیں ہے اور نہ ہلاک غالب کا خوف ہے تو زخم کی گہرائی ایک سلائی سے ناپی جائے پھر اسی کے بقدر ایک لو ہا تیز کیا جائے پس اس سے اتنی مقدار کاٹ دی جائے جو اس نے کاٹا تھی پس استیفاء قصاص متحقق ہو جائے گا۔ تشریح موضحہ کے بعد جو زخم مذکور ہیں ان میں تو بالا اتفاق قصاص نہیں ہے۔ اور جو زخم کہ ایک سلائی سے زخم کی گہرائی کی پیمائش کر لی جائے جتنی اس کی گہرائی ہو اتنا ہی بڑا تیز دھار والا لوہا لے کر اتنا ہی کاٹ دیا جائے جتنا اس کا کٹا ہوا ہے لہذا مساوات ہوگئی۔ 1- تنبیہ امام اول بین زیاد نے روایت کیا میں امام صاحب سے قول اول کو حسن بن زیاد نے روایت کیا ہے اگر ظاہر الروایہ میں قصاص واجب ہوگا اور اصح یہی ہے۔ زیلعی ص ۱۳۳ ج ۶، سلب الانبر [؟] ص ۵۵۷ ج ۲ ۔ تنبیه - ۲ مگر سمحاق میں بالا جماع قصاص نہ ہو گا جیسے موضحہ سے بعد والے تین میں بالا جماع قصاص نہیں ہے۔ سلب 11 برس [؟] ۵۵۷ ج ۲
Statement: Qisas is not applicable in the other nine wounds except mudihah; rather, hukumat al-adl is applied because qisas requires equality and it is not possible here since these wounds have no defined limit where the knife can stop. This reasoning is common to all. For the three wounds after mudihah (hashimah, munqilah, ammah), the reason for no qisas is also that they involve bone fracture, and it has passed that there is no qisas in bones. In summary, according to Abu Hanifa's narration, there is no qisas in the six wounds above mudihah nor in the three after. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, there is qisas in wounds before mudihah: this is a narration from Abu Hanifa, and Muhammad says in al-Asl – and it is Zahir al-Riwayah – qisas is obligatory in pre-mudihah wounds because equality can be considered, as there is no bone breakage nor dominant fear of death, so its depth is measured with a probe, then a piece of iron is sharpened to that measure, and with it he cuts the amount that he cut, so qisas is fulfilled. Commentary: In wounds after mudihah, there is consensus on no qisas. For pre-mudihah wounds, on one side is Zahir al-Riwayah, and on the other a narration from Abu Hanifa that there is no qisas. Zahir al-Riwayah is what Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut: qisas is taken in the six pre-mudihah wounds because there is no bone fracture and there is no dominant fear of death from such minor wounds, so equality is possible. The method of equality is to measure the depth of the wound with a probe, then take an iron tool with a sharp edge of that depth and cut as much as was cut. Note 1: The first saying from Imam Abu Hanifa is narrated by Hasan ibn Ziyad; if according to Zahir al-Riwayah, qisas is obligatory and this is the soundest. Zaylai vol.6 p.133, S.... p.557 vol.2. Note 2: However, in simhaq, there is consensus that qisas does not apply, just as in the three after mudihah there is consensus on no qisas.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage covers an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qisas (retaliation) for wounds that are less severe than mudihah (a wound that bares the bone). The core issue is whether equality (musawat) can be achieved in such wounds. According to one narration from Abu Hanifa (transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad), qisas is not applied because these wounds have no defined limit or end point where the knife can stop, making exact retaliation impossible. Instead, hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation) is given. However, according to Zahir al-Riwayah (the apparent transmitted position, as recorded by Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut), qisas is obligatory in the six wounds below mudihah. The reason is that these wounds do not involve bone fracture nor pose a dominant risk of death, so equality can be achieved by measuring the wound's depth with a probe and then cutting an identical amount. The passage then elaborates on the method: the wound is probed, an iron tool is sharpened to that exact depth, and the same quantity is cut. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Zahir al-Riwayah view, making qisas applicable. The author also notes that there is consensus (ijma') that no qisas applies in wounds above mudihah (hashimah, munqilah, ammah) because they involve bone fracture, and in the wound called simhaq (a scalp wound) there is also consensus that qisas is not applied.

Key Terms
موضحہ (mudihah): A wound that bares the bone (lays the bone open).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily injury, exacting an equivalent wound.
مساوات (musawat): Equality between the injury inflicted and the retaliation, a prerequisite for qisas.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent/well-known transmitted position of the Hanafi school, recorded in the six core books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the condition that makes qisas permissible in pre-mudihah wounds?
A) The wound must be on the head or face.
B) The wound must not involve bone fracture or cause dominant fear of death.
C) The wound must be intentional (amd).
D) The wound must be deeper than mudihah.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is wajib in pre-mudihah wounds according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, as equality can be achieved through measurement.

Qisas — Retaliation
intermediate

Qisas for Finger Cut Causing Paralysis: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas for finger injury with unintended paralysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on qisas for finger injuries with unintended paralysis, and explain the role of sirayah in creating doubt (shubha) that blocks qisas.

Core Idea
When injury to one finger paralyzes another, sirayah creates shubha: Abu Hanifa cancels qisas entirely; the Sahibayn split qisas and arsh.

The Hanafi school is united on the principles of qisas, but within it there are important disagreements on how to apply them when an intentional act has unintended consequences. This passage presents a classic example: cutting one finger causes paralysis in the adjacent finger. Does qisas apply to the cut finger? To the paralyzed one? The answer depends on whether the two injuries are considered a single act (due to sirayah) or separate acts, and this ikhtilaf shows the depth of Hanafi reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify the exact situation: a person intentionally cuts one finger of another, and as a result the adjacent finger becomes paralyzed. Note that the paralysis is unintended.
The case assumes intentionality for the cut, but the paralysis is a consequential effect.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling and reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that no qisas is due for either finger. His reasoning: the strong connection between fingers means the cut's effect 'transfers' (sirayah) to the second finger, making both injuries part of one direct act. This creates a shubha (doubt) about the precise scope of intent, and qisas requires certainty.
For Abu Hanifa, sirayah turns what might be seen as two acts into one continuous act.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's ruling and reasoning
Abu Yusuf, Muhammad (the Sahibayn), Zufar, and Hasan hold that qisas applies to the first finger (directly cut) and compensation (arsh) for the second (paralyzed indirectly). They distinguish between a direct act (mubasharah) and an indirect cause (tasbib).
For them, the first act is clearly intentional and direct, so qisas is wajib; the second is a consequence requiring arsh.
4
Analyze the rebuttals and distinctions
The text anticipates two objections: (1) if a single bullet hits two persons, would we also say no qisas? No, because there is no sirayah between separate persons. (2) If after cutting a finger, the hand trembles and a knife drops on another finger, would the first cut also be free from qisas? No, because the second act is not a completion of the first, but a separate event. These show the limits of the sirayah argument.
The key is whether the second injury is a natural and direct consequence (sirayah) or an independent act.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the victim receives arsh for both fingers (since no qisas). Under the Sahibayn, the victim may demand qisas on the first finger (if conditions permit) and arsh for the second. This difference affects judicial rulings and the rights of the victim.
The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) in the madhhab is often the Sahibayn's view, being more famous and practical.

Source Text

ایک انگلی کاٹی برابر والی انگلی شل ہوگئی قصاص ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
وان قطع اصبعا فشلت الى جنبها اخرى فلا قصاص فى شئ من ذالك عند ابي حنيفة وقالا وزفر حسن يقتص من الأولى وفى الثانية ارشها والوجه من الجانبين قد ذكرناه قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر ایک انگلی کاٹ دی پس اس کے پہلو میں دوسری انگلی شل ہوگئی تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ان دونوں میں سے کسی میں قصاص نہیں ہے اور صاحبین اور زفر اور حسن نے فرمایا کہ اول کا قصاص لیا جائے گا۔ اور دوسری میں اس کا ارش ہو گا اور جانبین کی دلیل وہی ہے جس کو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔
پھر جب ایک گولی سے دوسرے ہیں وہاں بھی یونہی کہو اور قصاص اول میں بھی واجب نہ کرو؟ یہ قیاس مع الفاروق ہے گفتگو گل واحد میں سرایت سے چل رہی ہے اور یہاں نہ محل واحد ہے اور نہ سرایت ہے کیونکہ ان میں یک کامرنا دوسرے کی سرایت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ تیر لگنے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اگر زید نے خالد کی ایک انگلی کاٹ دی پھر زید کے ہاتھ کے اضطراب کی وجہ سے اس کے ہاتھ پر چھری گر گئی جو خالد کی دوسری انگلی پر گری تو یہاں بھی کہو کہ جیسے دوسری انگلی میں قصاص واجب نہیں ہے اسی طرح پہلی انگلی میں بھی قصاص واجب نہیں ہے؟ یہ بھی قصاص مع الفارق ہے کیونکہ یہاں دوسرا فعل اول کا اثر نہیں ہے کہ ثانی کو اول کا تتمہ قرار دیا جا سکے تو یہاں اول میں وہی شبہ پیدا نہیں ہوا کیونکہ یہ دونوں فعل متفائز ہیں اور صورت مذکورہ میں ثانی اول کی سرایت کی وجہ سے ہے تو ثانی کو اوّل کا تتمہ قرار دیا جا سکتا ہے۔
یہاں بھی فریقین کی دلیلیں وہی ہیں جو اوپر والے مسئلہ میں تھیں
If someone cut a finger and the adjacent finger became paralyzed: is qisas required or not? Statements of the jurists. And if he cut a finger and the adjacent finger became paralyzed, then according to Abu Hanifa there is no qisas for any of them. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, and Hasan said: qisas is taken for the first, and for the second there is compensation (arsh). The evidence from both sides we have already mentioned. Then: when from a single bullet two are hit, do you also say the same and not impose qisas for the first? This is an invalid analogy because the discussion there is about a single limb with transference, whereas here neither is a single limb nor transference, because the second is not due to transference from the first but due to being hit by the arrow. If Zayd cut Khalid's one finger, then due to trembling of his hand a knife fell on Khalid's second finger: would you also say that just as qisas is not wajib for the second finger, similarly qisas is not wajib for the first? This too is an invalid analogy because here the second act is not an effect of the first that it could be considered a completion of the first; thus no doubt arises in the first act because these two acts are separate. In the mentioned case, the second is due to transference from the first, so the second can be considered a completion of the first. Here too, the proofs of the two parties are the same as in the previous issue.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qisas (retaliation) when an intentional injury to one finger causes paralysis in an adjacent finger. The base matn states the ruling from Al-Quduri: According to Abu Hanifa, no qisas is required for either finger because the unintended paralysis creates a doubt (shubha) that prevents qisas, treating the entire incident as one direct act due to the strong connection between the fingers. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), along with Zufar and Hasan (a Basran scholar), qisas applies to the first finger (which was directly cut) and compensation (arsh) for the second (which was paralyzed indirectly). The text then refutes possible objections by distinguishing this case from others: unlike a single bullet hitting two persons (where there is no transference), here the paralysis is a direct consequence (sirayah) of the cut, so the second act is considered a completion of the first, creating a shubha in Abu Hanifa's view. The proofs are stated to be the same as discussed in a prior issue (likely referring to the head wound case). The passage follows the order: ruling, then distinction from other scenarios, then reference to established evidence.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional injury, applicable to limbs and wounds where possible.
ارش (arsh): Fixed monetary compensation for injuries not subject to qisas or diyah (e.g., for a paralyzed finger).
سرایت (sirayah): Transference of effect from one injury to another, treating the second as a direct consequence of the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when cutting one finger causes paralysis in an adjacent finger, what is the ruling on qisas?
A) Qisas for the first finger only
B) Qisas for both fingers
C) No qisas for either finger
D) Compensation (arsh) for the first, qisas for the second

Key Takeaway
Whether sirayah creates a shubha that blocks qisas on the first act depends on how the second injury arises—a key intra-Hanafi dispute with practical consequences for qisas and arsh.
